Why Is It Called Kalām?
Historical account and enumeration of reasons for naming kalām.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical circumstances that led to the codification of kalām and the five reasons scholars gave for naming it 'kalām'.

Core Idea
The name 'kalām' reflects both its dialectical method and the central controversy over divine speech.

Before we dive into the theological arguments of kalām, it's helpful to know how this science got its name and why it was developed. In this passage, the author gives us a brief history of early Islamic scholarship and then lists five reasons why this discipline was called 'kalām'. Understanding these reasons will give you insight into the nature of kalām as a science that thrives on debate and precise reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Historical background
Read the first part of the passage which describes why the early generations didn't need to codify rulings, and what changed that led to the development of kalām.
Notice the contrast between the early simplicity and later need for systematic theology.
2
Identify the five reasons
After the historical context, the author lists five distinct reasons for naming the science 'kalām'. Find each one and note how they relate to the practice of the science.
The reasons are introduced with phrases like 'because' (لأن).
3
Reflect on the naming
Consider why the name 'kalām' stuck, especially compared to earlier names like 'al-fiqh al-akbar'. What does the name tell us about the method of this science?
The name highlights the centrality of discourse and argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكانت الأوائل ببركة صحبة النبي له وقرب العهد بزمانه وسماع الأخبار منه، ومشاهدة الآثار مع قلة الوقائع والاختلافات، وسهولة المراجعة إلى الثقات مستغنين عن تدوين الأحكام، وترتيبها أبواباً وفصولاً، وتكثير المسائل فروعاً وأصولاً إلى أن ظهر اختلاف الآراء، والميل إلى البدع والأهواء؛ وكثرت الفتاوى والواقعات، وأمست الحاجة فيها إلى زيادة نظر والتفات فأخذ أرباب النظر والاستدلال في استنباط الأحكام وبذلوا جهدهم في تحقيق عقائد الإسلام وأقبلوا على تمهيد أصولها وقوانينها وتلخيص حججها وبراهينها، وتدوين المسائل بأدلتها، والشبه بأجوبتها، وسموا العلم باسم الفقه، وخصوا الاعتقاديات باسم الفقه الأكبر والأكثرون خصوا العمليات باسم الفقه، والاعتقاديات بعلم التوحيد والصفات تسمية بأشهر أجزائه وأشرفها وبعلم الكلام، لأن مباحثه كانت مصدرة بقولهم: الكلام في كذا وكذا ولأن أشهر الاختلافات فيه كانت مسألة كلام الله تعالى أنه قديم أو حادث، ولأنه يورث قدرة على الكلام في تحقيق الشرعيات كالمنطق في الفلسفيات، ولأنه كثر فيه من الكلام مع المخالفين والرد عليهم ما لم يكثر في غيره. ولأنه لقوة أدلته صار كأنه هو الكلام. سمي الكلام كلاماً لأنهم كانوا يصدرون مباحثه بقولهم: الكلام في كذا أو لأن صفة الكلام فيه أشهر ما وقع الاختلاف فيه أو لأنه يورث القدرة على الكلام في سائر الشرعيات وكان يسمى أولاً: الفقه الأكبر حين دونوه.
And the early generations, by virtue of the companionship of the Prophet ﷺ and the closeness of the era to his time, and hearing reports from him, and witnessing effects, along with the fewness of occurrences and differences, and the ease of referring to trustworthy persons, were independent of codifying rulings and arranging them in chapters and sections, and multiplying issues as branches and principles, until differences of opinions appeared, and inclination towards innovations and desires; and fatwas and incidents became numerous, and the need for increased consideration and attention arose. So the masters of reasoning and inference began to deduce rulings and exerted their efforts in verifying the beliefs of Islam, and set about establishing its principles and laws and summarizing its proofs and evidences, and compiling issues with their proofs and doubts with their answers. And they named the science with the name 'fiqh', and they specified the doctrinal matters with the name 'al-fiqh al-akbar' (the greater fiqh). But the majority specified the practical matters with the name 'fiqh', and the doctrinal matters with 'the science of tawḥīd and attributes', naming it by its most famous and noble parts, and by 'the science of kalām', because its investigations used to begin with their saying: 'the discussion (al-kalām) about such and such', and because the most famous differences in it were the issue of the speech of Allah Almighty, whether it is eternal or created, and because it gives the ability to speak concerning the verification of religious matters, like logic does in philosophical matters, and because there occurred in it much discussion with opponents and refutation of them, not occurring to this extent in other sciences, and because due to the strength of its proofs it became as if it is itself the speech (al-kalām). It was called kalām because they used to begin its investigations with their saying: 'the discussion about such and such', or because the attribute of speech in it was the most famous subject of disagreement, or because it gives the ability to speak in all religious matters. And it was first called 'al-fiqh al-akbar' when they compiled it.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage provides a historical account of the development of Islamic sciences and the naming of kalām. The author describes that the early generations (al-awāʾil) did not need to codify rulings because of their proximity to the Prophet, few disputes, and easy access to reliable sources. However, as differences of opinion emerged and innovations arose, scholars began to systematically deduce rulings and compile proofs. They originally called the entire science 'fiqh', but later distinguished between practical rulings (fiqh) and doctrinal matters (al-fiqh al-akbar or 'ilm al-tawḥīd wa-l-ṣifāt). The science was also called 'ilm al-kalām for several reasons: (1) Its investigations began with the phrase 'al-kalām fī kadhā' (the discussion about such and such). (2) The most famous controversy in it was regarding the attribute of speech (kalām) of Allah—whether it was eternal or created. (3) It enables one to speak (capability in discourse) on religious matters, analogous to logic in philosophy. (4) It involved extensive debate and refutation of opponents, more than other sciences. (5) Its strong proofs made it as if it were 'speech' itself. The author notes it was initially called 'al-fiqh al-akbar' when first compiled.

Key Terms
الفقه الأكبر
علم التوحيد والصفات
الكلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The name 'kalām' means 'speech' because it deals with the physical speech of humans.
Correction: The name is derived from the dialectical method (opening with 'al-kalām fī...') and the central debate over God's speech (kalām Allāh). It does not refer to human speech in general.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which reason for naming the science 'kalām' relates to the opening phrase used by scholars?
A) It gives the ability to speak about religious matters.
B) Its investigations began with 'al-kalām fī kadhā'.
C) The most famous controversy was about God's speech.
D) It involves much debate with opponents.

Key Takeaway
The science of kalām was named after its method of dialectical investigation (opening with 'kalām fī...') and the central controversy over the divine attribute of speech, reflecting its argumentative nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever neglected to learn the proofs of your faith, thinking that simple belief is enough? If so, how can you ignore the command to 'call to the way of your Lord with wisdom and goodly exhortation'? What step will you take this week to strengthen your ability to defend the truth?
?
This science was born from the need to answer doubts. Is there a doubt in your heart—about Allah, the Prophet, or the unseen—that you have been avoiding? Are you willing to confront it with evidence from revelation and reason, or will you let it fester?
?
The scholars engaged in extensive debate with opponents. Is your love for comfort and avoiding conflict preventing you from speaking truth when it is challenged? Would you rather be silent than risk a difficult conversation? Ask Allah for courage, and commit to speaking one truth this week even if it is hard.

Why Is It Called 'Ilm al-Kalam? Five Reasons
Lists five reasons why this science is called al-kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five distinct reasons scholars gave for naming Islamic theology 'Ilm al-Kalam, and see how each reason reflects an aspect of the discipline.

Core Idea
The name 'al-Kalam' captures the science's method, key debate, utility, polemical nature, and proof strength.

You've likely heard the term 'Ilm al-Kalam' but wondered why it's called 'the science of speech'. The passage you're about to read gives five independent reasons, each shedding light on the nature of this discipline. As you work through the lesson, notice how each reason highlights a different feature of the science.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Get the overall sense of the five reasons.
2
Identify each reason
Note the five separate justifications. Pay attention to the distinct emphasis of each: opening phrase, debate on God's Speech, utility, refutation frequency, and proof strength.
3
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
Understand that these are not steps of a single etymology but separate parallel reasons. The list is often misread as a single explanation.
See the misconception field.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسموا العلم باسم الفقه، وخصوا الاعتقاديات باسم الفقه الأكبر والأكثرون خصوا العمليات باسم الفقه، والاعتقاديات بعلم التوحيد والصفات تسمية بأشهر أجزائه وأشرفها وبعلم الكلام، لأن مباحثه كانت مصدرة بقولهم: الكلام في كذا وكذا ولأن أشهر الاختلافات فيه كانت مسألة كلام الله تعالى أنه قديم أو حادث، ولأنه يورث قدرة على الكلام في تحقيق الشرعيات كالمنطق في الفلسفيات، ولأنه كثر فيه من الكلام مع المخالفين والرد عليهم ما لم يكثر في غيره. ولأنه لقوة أدلته صار كأنه هو الكلام دون ما عداه كما يقال للأقوى من الكلامين هذا هو الكلام.
They named the science 'fiqh', and they specifically called the beliefs 'the greater fiqh', and most people specifically called the practical matters 'fiqh', and the beliefs 'the science of tawhid and attributes', naming it after its most famous and noble parts, and 'the science of kalam', because its investigations used to begin with their saying: 'The discussion (kalam) is about such and such', and because the most famous disagreements in it were the question of the Speech of God Almighty—whether it is eternal or created, and because it gives ability to speak (kalam) in verifying religious matters, just as logic does in philosophical matters, and because there is much speech (kalam) in it with opponents and refuting them, not found to this extent in other sciences, and because due to the strength of its proofs it became as if it was the speech (kalam) itself, just as the stronger of two statements is called 'this is the speech (kalam)'.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage enumerates the reasons why the science of Islamic theology is called 'al-kalam'. The author begins by noting that initially all religious knowledge was called 'fiqh', but later the practical part retained 'fiqh' while beliefs were called 'the greater fiqh', 'tawhid and attributes', and 'al-kalam'. Then he lists five reasons for the name 'al-kalam': (1) their discussions used to begin with the phrase 'al-kalam fi kadha' (discussion about such and such); (2) the most famous debate in this science was about the attribute of Speech (kalam) of God—whether eternal or created; (3) it grants ability to speak (kalam) in verifying religious matters, similar to logic in philosophy; (4) there is much speech (kalam) with opponents and refutation, more than in other sciences; (5) because of the strength of its proofs, it is as if it is the speech (kalam) itself, just as the stronger of two statements is called 'this is the speech' (i.e., the decisive word). Each reason highlights a different aspect of the science's identity.

Key Terms
علم الكلام
الفقه الأكبر
التوحيد والصفات
كلام الله
الأدلة اليقينية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The five reasons are steps of a single explanation for the name.
Correction: Each reason independently justifies the name; they are not cumulative stages.

Checkpoint
How many reasons does the author give for calling this science 'al-kalam'?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
The science of kalam is named after multiple characteristic features, not from a single origin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The science of kalam is named for its power to produce decisive speech. When you speak about your faith, do your words carry the weight of evidence and conviction? What would need to change in your study of Islam for your speech to become truly decisive?
?
One reason for the name is the abundance of speech with opponents. When you encounter someone who challenges your beliefs, do you engage with the goal of truth or with the aim of winning? Ask yourself: am I willing to be corrected if my position is weak?
?
God's Speech (the Quran) is central to this science. Do you treat the Quran as the ultimate authority in your life, or do your own desires and opinions often override it? Commit to one specific way you will submit to God's speech today.

Definition of Kalam: Certainty and Scope
Defines kalam as knowledge of religious beliefs from certain proofs and explains scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise definition of the science of kalam, including its requirement of certain proofs and its scope relative to fiqh and other knowledge.

Core Idea
Kalam is the certain knowledge of religious beliefs, excluding conjecture and blind imitation.

This passage establishes the foundational definition of kalam. It begins by emphasizing the necessity of certainty (yaqin) in its proofs, contrasting with practical fiqh where conjecture is acceptable. This rigorous standard sets kalam apart as a discipline of reasoned conviction about creed. The author then clarifies what falls within and outside this definition, offering a comprehensive understanding of the science.

Guided Path
1
Understand the role of certainty
Notice the emphasis on yaqin and why conjecture is rejected in beliefs. This is the key criterion for kalam's proofs.
The text says: 'لا عبرة بالظن في الاعتقاديات بل في العمليات'.
2
Follow the definition formation
Read how the author combines 'religious-legal rules concerning beliefs' with 'certain proofs' to form the core definition.
Definition: 'العلم بالقواعد الشرعية الاعتقادية المكتسب من أدلتها اليقينية'.
3
Connect to 'greater fiqh'
See the relationship to the concept of 'greater fiqh' and how kalam encompasses the foundational beliefs.
The author equates kalam with 'الفقه الأكبر' in matters of belief.
4
Identify exclusions and inclusions
Examine the list of what is excluded (e.g., innate knowledge, muqallid's belief) and included (Companions' kalam) to grasp the boundaries.
Excluded: non-religious matters, practical fiqh, God's knowledge, Prophet's knowledge, muqallid's belief.
5
Appreciate the faculty aspect
Understand the reference to al-Mawaqif that kalam is a science enabling one to derive beliefs, emphasizing it as an acquired skill.
The passage ends with: 'علم يقتدر معه' indicating a faculty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعتبروا في أدلتها اليقين لأنه لا عبرة بالظن في الاعتقاديات بل في العمليات فظهر: أنه العلم بالقواعد الشرعية الاعتقادية المكتسب من أدلتها اليقينية. وهذا هو معنى العقائد الدينية أي المنسوبة إلى دين محمد [؟] على الشرع أم لا، وسواء كان من الدين في الواقع ككلام أهل الحق أم لا، ككلام المخالفين. وصار قولنا هو: العلم بالعقائد الدينية عن الأدلة اليقينية مناسباً لقولهم في الفقه إنه العلم بالأحكام الشرعية الفرعية عن أدلتها التفصيلية. وموافقاً لما نقل عن بعض عظماء الملة: إن الفقه معرفة النفس مالها وما عليها، وأن ما يتعلق منها بالاعتقاديات هو الفقه الأكبر. وخرج العلم بغير الشرعيات وبالشرعيات الفرعية، وعلم الله تعالى، وعلم الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم بالاعتقاديات، وكذا اعتقاد المقلد فيمن يسميه علماً، ودخل علم علماء الصحابة بذلك، فإنه كلام وإن لم يسم في ذلك الزمان بهذا الاسم. وذلك إذا كان متعلقاً بالعقائد بقدر الطاقة البشرية، مكتسباً من النظر في الأدلة اليقينية، أو كان ملكة يتعلق بها، بأن يكون عندهم من المآخذ والشرائط ما يكفيهم في استحضار العقائد على ما هو المراد بقولنا العلم بالعقائد عن الأدلة. وإلى المعنى الأخير يشير قول صاحب المواقف أنه علم يقتدر معه.
And they considered certainty in its proofs because there is no consideration for conjecture in beliefs, but rather in practical matters. So it became clear: it is the knowledge of the religious-legal rules concerning beliefs, acquired from their certain proofs. And this is the meaning of 'religious creeds', i.e., those attributed to the religion of Muhammad [؟] whether dependent on revelation or not, and whether they are actually from the religion like the speech of the people of truth or not, like the speech of opponents. And our statement 'knowledge of religious creeds from certain proofs' became appropriate to their statement in fiqh that it is knowledge of subsidiary legal rulings from their detailed proofs, and in agreement with what is transmitted from some great men of the community: 'Fiqh is the soul's knowledge of what is for it and against it, and that which relates to beliefs is the greater fiqh.' And there is excluded: knowledge of non-religious matters, subsidiary religious matters, the knowledge of God Almighty and the knowledge of the Messenger صلى الله عليه وسلم concerning beliefs, and likewise the belief of a muqallid (imitative follower) from what is called knowledge. And there is included: the knowledge of the Companions in that matter, for it is kalam even if it was not called by this name in that time. And that is when it is related to beliefs to the extent of human capacity, acquired from reflection on certain proofs, or being a faculty related to it, such that they have from the principles and conditions what suffices them in recalling the beliefs according to what is intended by our statement 'knowledge of beliefs from proofs'. And to the latter meaning refers the statement of the author of al-Mawaqif that it is 'a science by which one is able'.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage defines the science of kalam. The author first asserts that certainty (yaqin) is required in its proofs, since conjecture (zann) is unacceptable in beliefs but permissible in practical law. From this, the definition emerges: 'knowledge of religious-legal rules concerning beliefs, acquired from their certain proofs.' He relates this to the earlier term 'greater fiqh'. Then he explains what is excluded and included: excluded are non-religious sciences, practical fiqh, the innate knowledge of God or the Prophet concerning beliefs, and the blind belief of a muqallid that is called knowledge only metaphorically. Included is the knowledge of the Companions about beliefs, even though in their time it was not called 'kalam', because it meets the criteria of being acquired from certain proofs or a faculty for producing such knowledge. Finally, he references the definition from al-Mawaqif ('a science by which one is able'), pointing to the meaning of kalam as an acquired faculty.

الأدلة اليقينية
الفقه الأكبر
المقلد
الملكة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Kalam can be based on conjectural proofs like practical fiqh.
Correction: The text explicitly states that conjecture has no place in beliefs; only certain proofs are accepted.

Checkpoint

D) No proofs required

Key Takeaway
Kalam is the certain knowledge of religious beliefs acquired from definitive proofs, distinct from practical fiqh and blind imitation.

?
The source says the Companion's knowledge of beliefs was kalam even though they didn't call it that. What step will you take this week to acquire certain knowledge in a topic you are unsure about?

Defining Ilm al-Kalam: Certainty and Doctrine
Definition of ilm al-kalam and its contrast with fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the traditional definition of ilm al-kalam distinguishes it from fiqh by requiring certain proofs in matters of belief.

Core Idea
Ilm al-kalam is the science of religious doctrines from certain proofs.

The author defines ilm al-kalam with precision, stressing that its proofs must be certain—unlike fiqh, which can rely on probability. This definition also clarifies what counts as kalam and what does not, such as the knowledge of the Prophet or blind imitation. Let's dive into the passage to see how this definition is built.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the requirement of certainty
Note the author's statement that in matters of belief (i'tiqadiyat) only certain proofs are acceptable; conjecture (zann) is invalid. This is a foundational principle.
This differs from fiqh, where conjecture can be sufficient.
2
Understand the definition formula
Read the definition: 'knowledge of religious doctrinal principles acquired from their certain proofs.' Identify each component: knowledge, religious doctrines, and acquisition from certain proofs.
The term 'acquisition' (iktisab) is crucial—it excludes innate or unquestioning belief.
3
Contrast with fiqh
Compare the definition of kalam with that of fiqh. The author notes that fiqh deals with subsidiary rulings from detailed proofs, while kalam deals with foundational doctrines from certain proofs.
Some great scholars called kalam the 'greater fiqh'.
4
Identify inclusions and exclusions
List what is excluded: non-religious matters, subsidiary rulings (fiqh proper), the knowledge of God and the Prophet, and the belief of a blind follower (taqlid). What is included: the knowledge of the Companions, even if not formally called kalam at their time.
The inclusion of the Companions shows that the essence of kalam is the faculty of proving doctrines, not the formal discipline.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دون ما عداه كما يقال للأقوى من الكلامين هذا هو الكلام، واعتبروا في أدلتها اليقين لأنه لا عبرة بالظن في الاعتقاديات بل في العمليات فظهر: أنه العلم بالقواعد الشرعية الاعتقادية المكتسب من أدلتها اليقينية وهذا هو معنى العقائد الدينية أي المنسوبة إلى دين محمد [؟] توقف على الشرع أم لا، وسواء كان من الدين في الواقع ككلام أهل الحق أم لا، ككلام المخالفين، وصار قولنا هو: العلم بالعقائد الدينية عن الأدلة اليقينية مناسباً لقولهم في الفقه إنه العلم بالأحكام الشرعية الفرعية عن أدلتها التفصيلية، وموافقاً لما نقل عن بعض عظماء الملة: إن الفقه معرفة النفس مالها وما عليها، وأن ما يتعلق منها بالاعتقاديات هو الفقه الأكبر وخرج العلم بغير الشرعيات وبالشرعيات الفرعية، وعلم الله تعالى، وعلم الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم بالاعتقاديات، وكذا اعتقاد المقلد فيمن يسميه علماً، ودخل علم علماء الصحابة بذلك، فإنه كلام وإن لم يكن، وسمي في ذلك الزمان بهذا الاسم، كما أن عملهم بالعمليات فقه، وإن لم يكن ثمة هذا التدوين والترتيب، وذلك إذا كان متعلقاً بالعقائد بقدر الطاقة البشرية، بجميع [؟] مكتسباً من النظر في الأدلة اليقينية، أو كان ملكة يتعلق بها، بأن يكون عندهم من المآخذ والشرائط ما يكفيهم في استحضار العقائد على ما هو المراد بقولنا العلم بالعقائد الأدلة، وإلى المعنى الأخير يشير قول صاحب المواقف أنه علم يقتدر معه
Apart from what is other than it, just as it is said of the stronger of two speeches: this is speech. And they considered certainty in its proofs because there is no consideration for conjecture in matters of belief, but rather in practical matters. So it became clear that it is knowledge of the religious doctrinal principles acquired from their certain proofs. And this is the meaning of religious doctrines, i.e., attributed to the religion of Muhammad [?] whether it depends on revelation or not, and whether it is in reality from the religion like the speech of the people of truth or not, like the speech of the opponents. And our saying: it is knowledge of religious doctrines from certain proofs became suitable to their saying in fiqh that it is knowledge of the subsidiary legal rulings from their detailed proofs, and in agreement with what has been transmitted from some great ones of the community: that fiqh is knowledge of the self of what it has and against it, and that what pertains to doctrines among them is the greater fiqh. And knowledge of non-religious matters and of subsidiary religious matters is excluded, as is the knowledge of God Most High and the knowledge of the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, concerning doctrines, and likewise the belief of the blind follower in what he calls knowledge. And the knowledge of the Companions concerning that is included, for it is kalam even if it was not called by this name in that time, just as their actions in practical matters are fiqh even if there was not yet this codification and arrangement. And that is if the object of knowledge is the doctrines to the extent of human capacity, [?] acquired from contemplation of certain proofs, or if it is a faculty by which they are obtained, so that they have from the sources and conditions enough to bring to mind the doctrines according to what is intended by our saying: knowledge of doctrines from proofs. And to the latter meaning refers the statement of the author of al-Mawaqif that it is a science by which one is able to prove religious doctrines.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage defines ilm al-kalam. The author states that the proofs must be certain because in matters of belief (i'tiqadiyat) conjecture is not valid, unlike in practical matters. Then he gives the definition: knowledge of religious doctrinal principles acquired from certain proofs. He explains that 'religious doctrines' are those attributed to the religion of Muhammad. He compares this to the definition of fiqh, noting that fiqh deals with subsidiary rulings and that some great scholars considered the study of doctrines to be the 'greater fiqh.' He then excludes other types of knowledge: non-religious matters, subsidiary religious matters (which belong to fiqh), the knowledge of God and the Prophet concerning doctrines (since it is not acquired), and the belief of a blind follower (which is not considered knowledge). He includes the knowledge of the Companions, even though it was not called kalam at the time, because it meets the criteria: it is acquired from certain proofs through their own reasoning or a faculty they had. Finally, he notes that this understanding aligns with the definition of al-Iji that kalam is a science by which one is able to prove religious doctrines.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That ilm al-kalam includes blind faith (taqlid) without proof.
Correction: The definition explicitly requires acquisition from proofs; taqlid is excluded because it lacks certain proof.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Ilm al-kalam is defined as knowledge of religious doctrines acquired from certain proofs, distinguishing it from fiqh and excluding blind imitation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Ibn Khaldun's Definition of Kalam
Ibn Khaldun's definition of ilm al-kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Khaldun's definition of ilm al-kalam as argumentation for religious beliefs using rational proofs and refutation of heretics.

Core Idea
Kalam defends faith with reason against innovation.

Ibn Khaldun offers a concise definition that captures the dual purpose of kalam: to affirm religious beliefs through rational argument and to refute those who deviate. This definition situates kalam in a combative but constructive role within the Islamic intellectual tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage from Ibn Khaldun
Read the Arabic sentence carefully, then the translation. Notice the two key functions mentioned.
Ibn Khaldun uses the term 'ilm' for kalam.
2
Identify the two components
Identify the positive component (argumentation for beliefs) and the negative component (refutation of heretics).
3
Understand rational proofs
Reflect on why Ibn Khaldun specifies 'rational proofs' as the means. Why is reason important in defending faith?
This connects kalam to logic and philosophy.
4
Contextualize the definition
Consider the historical background of defending the Salaf and Ahl al-Sunna against innovators.
This shows kalam's role in preserving orthodoxy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بری ابن خلدون : أنه علم يتضمن الحجاج على العقائد الإيمانية بالأدلة العقلية. والرد على المبتدعة المنحرفين في الاعتقادات عن مذهب السلف وأهل السنة (مقدمة ابن خلدون ص ٤٥٨). وقال الفارابي : إن الكلام صناعة يقتدر بها الإنسان على نصرة الأفعال والآراء المحددة التي صرح بها واضع الملة وتزييف كل ما خالف من الأقاويل (إحصاء العلوم ص ۷۱ - ۷۲).
Ibn Khaldun says: It is a science that comprises argumentation for religious beliefs with rational proofs, and refutation of heretical innovators who deviate in beliefs from the way of the Salaf and Ahl al-Sunna. And al-Farabi said: Kalam is a craft by which a person is able to support the specific actions and opinions that the founder of the religion has declared, and to falsify everything that opposes them from among the sayings.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage presents two classical definitions. Ibn Khaldun's definition emphasizes the role of rational proofs (adilla 'aqliyya) and the refutation of heretics. Al-Farabi's definition highlights the defensive and supportive nature of kalam as a craft (sina'a) used to uphold the teachings of the religion and to refute opposition. Both definitions agree on the apologetic and argumentative function of kalam.

Key Terms
الحجاج
الأدلة العقلية
المبتدعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That kalam is purely speculative without any connection to defending faith.
Correction: Ibn Khaldun's definition shows kalam is fundamentally about defending religious beliefs.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Khaldun, what are the two components of ilm al-kalam?
A) Argumentation for religious beliefs and refutation of heretics.
B) Study of logic and grammar.
C) Seeking inner spiritual knowledge.
D) Legal reasoning.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Khaldun defines kalam as a science that uses rational arguments to support Islamic beliefs and refute heresy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a modern challenge to your faith—like atheism, materialism, or skepticism—do you actively seek rational arguments to defend your beliefs, or do you rely on emotional comfort? How can you emulate the kalam methodology Ibn Khaldun describes, starting today?
?
Are you more focused on refuting what others believe wrong, or on building your own convictions with reasoned evidence? This passage presents both. Which one do you neglect, and what concrete step will you take this week to strengthen that side?
?
If you were asked by a sincere seeker why you believe in God and the truth of Islam, could you provide a rational argument from your own understanding—not just quoting scholars? If not, what prevents you from internalizing the rational proofs that this science demands?

Al-Farabi's Definition of Kalam
Al-Farabi's definition of ilm al-kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Farabi's characterization of ilm al-kalam as a craft for supporting the religion founder's teachings and refuting opposition.

Core Idea
Kalam is the craft of defending revealed doctrine rationally.

Al-Farabi, a philosopher, offers a definition that views kalam as a practical craft (sina'a) with a clear purpose: to defend the specific actions and opinions laid down by the founder of the religion and to falsify anything contrary. This definition highlights the instrumental role of kalam in preserving orthodoxy.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Farabi's definition
Read the Arabic sentence and its translation. Notice the term 'craft' (sina'a).
Al-Farabi uses 'sina'a' to emphasize skill.
2
Identify the two functions
Find the two tasks: supporting the founder's declarations and falsifying opposing sayings.
3
Reflect on 'craft'
Consider what it means for kalam to be a craft. What skills does it require?
This suggests kalam is learned and practiced.
4
Compare with Ibn Khaldun
Think about how al-Farabi's definition differs from Ibn Khaldun's. Does one focus more on method?
Both are complementary.

Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage presents two classical definitions. Ibn Khaldun's definition emphasizes the role of rational proofs (adilla 'aqliyya) and the refutation of heretics. Al-Farabi's definition highlights the defensive and supportive nature of kalam as a craft (sina'a) used to uphold the teachings of the religion and to refute opposition. Both definitions agree on the apologetic and argumentative function of kalam.

Key Terms
الصناعة
واضع الملة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That kalam is purely philosophical speculation divorced from religious authority.
Correction: Al-Farabi ties kalam directly to defending the founder's declarations.

Checkpoint
How does al-Farabi describe the function of kalam?
A) It argues rationally for beliefs.
B) It supports the founder's actions and opinions and falsifies opposition.
C) It explores metaphysical truths independent of revelation.
D) It is a method for inner purification.

Key Takeaway
Al-Farabi defines kalam as a craft for defending the religion's specific teachings and refuting contrary views.

?
Al-Farabi says kalam enables you to falsify opposing sayings. When someone raises an objection to your faith, do you feel equipped to respond, or do you avoid the conversation? What does that say about your commitment to truth?
?
Think of a time you heard a claim that contradicts Islam. Did you have the skill to falsify it, or did you remain silent? What will you do to change that starting today?

Defending the Definition of Kalam: The Problem of Qudra (Power)
The author defends al-Iji's definition against objections about other sciences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Iji's definition of kalam is defended against objections regarding the inclusion of other sciences and the status of power after doctrines are proven.

Core Idea
The definition of kalam is carefully worded to avoid implying that the science itself creates power.

Al-Iji defined kalam as a science by which one is able to prove religious doctrines. But this raises problems: does it include grammar and logic? And is it still applicable after the doctrines are already proven? In this passage, the author clarifies the meaning and defends the precision of the definition by explaining terms and addressing objections.

Guided Path
1
Understand 'proving doctrines'
Read how the author explains the meaning of 'proving doctrines' as acquiring them, verifying them, and being able to defend them against opponents.
This sets the stage for the definition's practical purpose.
2
Notice the word change
Al-Iji changed 'yqtadir bihi' to 'yqtadir mahu' to avoid implying that the science itself is the cause of power. Understand the theological reason: all power is from God.
This is a subtle but crucial linguistic choice.
3
Identify the objections
The passage presents two main objections: the definition overincludes other sciences (grammar, logic) and underincludes kalam after doctrines are proven (since no power remains).
These are standard critiques of definitions.
4
Learn the answer
The author answers by clarifying that the definition means the science with which power is customarily obtained, even if not permanently. Kalam is unique in this property.
Customary occurrence ('jari al-ada') is a key concept.
5
Address the logic objection
The author further addresses the claim that logic has an entry into power, arguing that kalam's role is distinct and the definition remains valid.
This shows the depth of the defense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومعنى إثبات العقائد تحصيلها واكتسابها بحيث يحصل الترقي من التقليد إلى التحقيق، أو إثباتها على الغير بحيث يتمكن من إلزام المعاندين أو إتقانها، وإحكامها بحيث لا تزلزلها شبه المبطلين، وعدل عن يقتدر به إلى يقتدر معه مبالغة في نفي الأسباب، واستناد الكل إلى خلق الله تعالى ابتداء على ما هو المذهب، وأورد على طرد تعريفه جميع العلوم الحاصلة عند الاقتدار من النحو والمنطق وغيرهما وعلى عكسه علم الكلام بعد إثبات العقائد لا نتفاء الاقتدار حينئذ والجواب أن المراد هو علم يحصل معه الاقتدار البتة بطريق جري العادة، أي يلزمه حصول الاقتدار لزوماً عادياً، وإن لم يبق ذلك الاقتدار دائماً، ولا خفاء في أن الكلام كذلك بخلاف سائر العلوم، وأما مجموع العلوم التي من جملتها الكلام فهو وإن كان كذلك فليس بعلم واحد بل بعلوم جمة، وقد يجاب بأن المراد ماله مدخل في الاقتدار أو ما يلزم معه الاقتدار ولو على بعض التقادير والكلام بعد الإثبات بهذه الحيثية بخلاف سائر العلوم، ويعترض بأن للمنطق مدخلاً في الاقتدار وإن لم يستقل به، والاقتدار لازم مع كل علم على تقدير مقارنته للكلام. نعم لو أريد ما يلزم معه الاقتدار في الجملة بحيث يكون له مدخل في ذلك خرج غير المنطق، وفيما ذكرنا غنية عن هذا، مع أن في إثبات المدخل إشعاراً بالسببية ولو قال يقتدر به وأراد الاستعقاب العادي، كما في إثبات العقائد بإيراد الحجج على ما هو المذهب في حصول النتيجة عقيب النظر لم يحتج إلى شيء من ذلك.
And the meaning of proving the doctrines is acquiring them and obtaining them such that ascension from taqlid to verification occurs, or proving them to others so that one is able to oblige the obstinate, or mastering them and strengthening them so that the doubts of the false do not shake them. And he turned from 'yqtadir bihi' to 'yqtadir mahu' as an exaggeration in negating [intermediate] causes, and the attribution of everything to the creation of God Most High from the beginning, as is the school. And an objection was raised against the includedness of his definition: all sciences that arise with power, like grammar, logic, and others, and against its exclusiveness: the science of kalam after proving doctrines because there is no power then. And the answer is that what is meant is a science with which power is necessarily obtained by way of customary occurrence, i.e., the attainment of power follows it in a customary manner, even if that power does not remain always. And it is not hidden that kalam is such, unlike other sciences. As for the totality of sciences that include kalam, even if it is such, it is not a single science but many sciences. And it may be answered that what is meant is that which has an entry into the power, or that with which power is obtained even on some suppositions, and kalam after proof is in this respect unlike other sciences. And it is objected that logic has an entry into power even if it is not independent, and power necessarily accompanies every science on the supposition of its conjunction with kalam. Yes, if what is intended is that with which power is obtained in general such that it has an entry in that, then other than logic would be excluded. And in what we have mentioned there is sufficiency regarding this, especially since in establishing an entry there is an indication of causality. And if he had said 'yqtadir bihi' and intended customary sequel, as in proving doctrines by adducing arguments according to the school regarding the attainment of the result consequent upon consideration, he would not have needed any of this.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage discusses al-Iji's definition that kalam is a science by which one is able to prove religious doctrines. The author explains the meaning of 'proving doctrines': attaining them meticulously, or proving them to others. He notes the deliberate word change from 'yqtadir bihi' to 'yqtadir mahu' to avoid implying that the science itself is the cause (since all power comes from God). Then an objection is raised: if the definition includes every science that gives power, then grammar and logic would be included; also, after kalam is already proven, one can no longer have the power to prove it, so the definition would not apply. The author answers that the definition means the science with which power is customarily obtained, not necessarily perpetually. He also addresses the objection that logic has some role, but the author argues that the definition's scope is limited to the specific science of kalam. The discussion shows the precision required in defining ilm al-kalam.

الاستدلال
التقليد
التحقيق
العادة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'yqtadir bihi' implies that the science itself creates power, independent of God.
Correction: The change to 'yqtadir mahu' emphasizes that the science is merely a customary means, not a cause; all power is from God.

Checkpoint

B) To negate any implication that the science itself is the cause of power, since all power is from God.
C) Because it is grammatically more correct.

Key Takeaway
The precise wording of al-Iji's definition excludes other sciences and affirms that power is atttained customarily through kalam, not by its own causality.

Defining Kalam and Addressing Objections
Sanusi defines ilm al-kalam and resolves objections about its scope and the role of capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the classical definition of ilm al-kalam is refined to address objections about its scope and the role of capacity.

Core Idea
Kalam is the science of conviction—not just belief, but defended conviction.

Sanusi presents the formal definition of ilm al-kalam and immediately anticipates potential objections. A good definition must be neither too broad nor too narrow, and the author shows how the choice of wording guards against both. This passage demonstrates the precision of kalam methodology itself: even defining the discipline requires the same rigorous reasoning it teaches.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the precise wording used by Sanusi.
Notice the shift from 'يقتدر به' to 'يقتدر معه'.
2
Understand three meanings of 'establishing beliefs'
The author explains that إثبات العقائد can mean personal acquisition from imitation to verification, teaching others to compel the obstinate, or perfecting beliefs against doubts.
Each meaning highlights a different aspect of kalam's purpose.
3
Identify the two objections
Find the objection about the definition being too broad (including grammar and logic) and too narrow (excluding kalam after beliefs are established). Note how they relate to 'طرد' and 'عكس'.
The objection challenges the definition's completeness.
4
Analyze the answers
See how Sanusi resolves each objection. He clarifies that kalam is accompanied by capacity by normal course, not permanently, and that the aggregate of sciences is not one science.
5
Reflect on the role of capacity
Consider why capacity (اقتدار) is central and how the concept of 'جري العادة' allows the definition to remain precise.
This connects to the Ash'ari emphasis on God as the sole cause.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

on establishing religious beliefs (العقائد الدينية) by adducing proofs (الحجج) and repelling doubts (الشبه). And the meaning of establishing beliefs (إثبات العقائد) is acquiring and obtaining them such that one rises from imitation (التقليد) to verification (التحقيق), or establishing them to others such that one is able to compel the obstinate, or perfecting and strengthening them such that the doubts of the falsifiers do not shake them. And he changed from 'by which one has capacity' (يقتدر به) to 'with which one has capacity' (يقتدر معه) as an exaggeration in negating causes, and the attribution of all to the creation of God, exalted, in the first instance according to the school. And an objection was raised against the universal applicability (طرد) of his definition that it includes all sciences obtained with capacity, such as grammar and logic and others, and against its converse (عكسه) that it excludes the science of kalam after establishing beliefs due to the absence of capacity then. The answer is that what is meant is a science with which capacity is certainly obtained by way of the normal course (جري العادة), i.e., capacity necessarily accompanies it by normal necessity, even if that capacity does not remain permanently. And it is not hidden that kalam is like that, unlike other sciences. As for the aggregate of sciences of which kalam is one, even if it is like that, it is not a single science but many sciences. And it may be answered that what is meant is that which has a role in capacity or that with which capacity follows even on some assumptions, and kalam after establishing beliefs is like that, unlike other sciences. And it is objected that logic has a role in capacity even if it does not suffice by itself, and capacity is necessary with every science on the assumption of its conjunction with kalam. Yes, if what is meant is that with which capacity follows in general such that it has a role in that, then other than logic would be excluded. In what we have mentioned there is sufficiency from this, especially since affirming a role implies causation. And if he had said 'by which one has capacity' and meant the customary consequence, as in establishing beliefs by adducing proofs according to the school that the result follows after reflection, he would not have needed any of this.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage presents the definition of ilm al-kalam, explains the meaning of 'establishing beliefs,' and then addresses two objections concerning the definition's scope and the role of capacity. The author begins by stating that kalam is the science of establishing religious beliefs by adducing proofs and repelling doubts. He then clarifies that 'establishing beliefs' can mean either acquiring them oneself (moving from imitation to verification) or proving them to others to compel opponents. The author notes a shift in phrasing from 'by which one has capacity' to 'with which one has capacity' to emphasize that all capacity is ultimately from God's creation, following the Ash'ari school. An objection is then raised: the definition is too broad (it includes grammar and logic, which also involve capacity) and too narrow (it excludes kalam after beliefs are established, since capacity is no longer needed). The author answers that the intended meaning is that kalam is a science normally accompanied by capacity, even if not permanently. For the aggregate of sciences including kalam, it is not one science but many, so the objection fails. A second objection argues that logic also plays a role in capacity. The author replies that if we mean a science with which capacity follows in general and has a role, then logic would be excluded (since it does not independently yield capacity). He concludes that the original phrasing using 'the customary consequence' suffices, as in the case of reflection leading to knowledge.

Misconception: Capacity (اقتدار) must be permanently present for a science to be kalam.
Correction: The author clarifies that capacity is normally accompanying (جري العادة), not permanent, and that is sufficient for the definition.

The definition of kalam is carefully crafted to be exact and exclusive, using the concept of normal accompaniment to resolve objections.

The Role of Subject Matter in Defining a Science
The author explains that the subject matter distinguishes sciences in essence and unifies their questions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the subject matter of a science is essential for distinguishing it in essence and unifying its questions.

Core Idea
The subject matter gives a science its identity and holds its questions together.

The author begins by stating the subject matter of kalam. He then explains the crucial role of the subject matter in defining a science, both conceptually and essentially. This passage lays the foundation for understanding how different sciences are distinguished and how their questions are unified.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening quote
Read the Arabic quote and translation. It defines the subject matter of kalam as 'things insofar as establishing them is connected to it.'
This is the matn statement.
2
Understand the two functions of subject matter
The author explains that the subject matter discriminates the science in essence (after the definition discriminates in concept) and provides a unifying aspect for its many questions.
Think of the subject as the core topic that all questions revolve around.
3
Reflect on unity of questions
Consider why knowing the subject matter helps prevent straying into unrelated topics when studying details.
The subject matter acts as a guide for what belongs to the science.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قال) وموضوعه العلوم من حيث يتعلق به إثباتها. أقول: اتفقت كلمة القوم على أن التمييز العلوم في أنفسها إنما هو بحسب تمايز الموضوعات، فناسب تصدير العلم ببيان الموضوع لإفادة لما به يتميز بحسب الذات بعد ما أفاد التعريف التمييز بحسب المفهوم، وأيضاً في معرفة جهة الوحدة للكثرة المطلوبة إحاطة بها إجمالاً بحيث إذا قصد تحصيل تفاصيلها لم ينصرف الطلب عما هو منها إلى ما ليس منها، ولا شك أن جهة وحدة مسائل العلم أولاً وبالذات هو الموضوع، إذ فيه اشتراكها وبه اتحادها على ما سنفصله، وتحقيق المقام أنهم لما حاولوا معرفة أحوال الأشياء بقدر الطاقة البشرية على ما هو المراد بالحكمة، وصنعوا الحقائق أنواعاً وأجناساً وغيرها، كالإنسان والحيوان والموجود، وبحثوا عن أحوالها المختصة وأثبتوها لها بالأدلة، فحصلت لهم قضايا كسبية محمولاتها أعراض ذاتية لتلك الحقائق، سموها بالمسائل، وجعلوا كل طائفة منها يرجع إلى واحد من تلك الأشياء، بأن تكون موضوعاتها نفسه أو جزءاً له أو نوعاً منه أو عرضاً ذاتياً له، علماً خاصاً يفرد.
He said: And its subject matter is the things, insofar as establishing them is connected to it. I say: The community agrees that the discrimination of sciences in themselves is only according to the differentiation of subject matters. So it is fitting to preface the science with an exposition of the subject matter, to convey that by which it is discriminated in essence after the definition conveyed discrimination in concept. Also, to know the aspect of unity for the multiplicity sought, achieving an encompassing grasp of it in summary, so that when one intends to obtain its details, the seeker does not turn away from what is part of it to what is not part of it. There is no doubt that the aspect of unity of the questions (مسائل) of a science, primarily and essentially, is the subject matter, for in it they share and by it they are united, as we will detail. The reality of the matter is that when they attempted to know the states of things to the extent of human capacity, as is meant by wisdom (الحكمة), and they arranged realities into species and genera and so on, such as human, animal, and existent, and they investigated their specific states and proved them for them by proofs, there resulted for them acquired propositions whose predicates are essential accidents (أعراض ذاتية) for those realities; they called them questions (مسائل). And they made each group of them refer back to one of those things, such that their subject matters are itself, or a part of it, or a species of it, or an essential accident of it, as a special science distinguished.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage discusses the subject matter (موضوع) of ilm al-kalam. The author first quotes the matn: 'Its subject matter is the things, insofar as establishing them is connected to it.' Then he comments ('I say') that scholars agree sciences are distinguished by their subject matters. Thus it is appropriate to begin a science by stating its subject matter, which gives the science its identity in essence (after the definition gave it conceptual identity). Moreover, knowing the subject provides a unifying aspect for the many questions of the science, enabling the student to have a holistic overview and not stray into unrelated topics. The author insists that the primary unifying factor of a science's questions is its subject matter, as questions share that subject and are united by it. He then provides a historical-epistemological explanation: scholars, in their pursuit of wisdom (الحكمة), investigated the states of things, classified realities into genera and species, and derived acquired propositions whose predicates are essential accidents (أعراض ذاتية) of those realities. These propositions are called questions (مسائل). They then grouped these questions under a single subject, which could be the subject itself, a part of it, a species of it, or an essential accident of it, thereby forming a distinct science. This explains how the subject matter of kalam—the things insofar as they relate to establishing beliefs—unifies its questions.

Key Terms
موضوع
مسائل
تمييز
جهة الوحدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To show the science's nobility
B) To define its questions and unify them
C) To list all possible topics
D) To prove the existence of God

Key Takeaway
The subject matter of a science is essential for distinguishing it in essence and for unifying its many questions under one coherent topic.

How the Questions of Kalam Are Derived from Realities
The author traces the epistemological process by which scholars derived propositions (masa'il) from realities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the epistemological process by which scholars derived the questions (masa'il) of kalam from the study of realities.

Core Idea
The questions of a science are acquired propositions whose predicates are essential accidents of the subject.

The author now delves into the epistemological genesis of the questions of a science. He explains how scholars, in their pursuit of wisdom, examined realities, categorized them, and derived propositions that form the questions of a distinct science. This passage connects the abstract concept of subject matter to the concrete content of kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the pursuit of wisdom
Read the Arabic and translation. The passage describes scholars attempting to know the states of things to the extent of human capacity.
This is the starting point: the desire for wisdom (al-hikmah).
2
Identify the stages of deriving questions
Note the steps: arranging realities into categories, investigating specific states, proving them with evidence, and resulting in propositions with essential accidents.
These propositions are called 'masa'il' (questions).
3
Understand the grouping into sciences
The final step is grouping related propositions under a single subject (the subject itself, part, species, or essential accident), forming a distinct science.
This shows how the subject matter organizes the questions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(قال) وموضوعه العلوم من حيث يتعلق به إثباتها. أقول: اتفقت كلمة القوم على أن التمييز العلوم في أنفسها إنما هو بحسب تمايز الموضوعات، فناسب تصدير العلم ببيان الموضوع لإفادة لما به يتميز بحسب الذات بعد ما أفاد التعريف التمييز بحسب المفهوم، وأيضاً في معرفة جهة الوحدة للكثرة المطلوبة إحاطة بها إجمالاً بحيث إذا قصد تحصيل تفاصيلها لم ينصرف الطلب عما هو منها إلى ما ليس منها، ولا شك أن جهة وحدة مسائل العلم أولاً وبالذات هو الموضوع، إذ فيه اشتراكها وبه اتحادها على ما سنفصله، وتحقيق المقام أنهم لما حاولوا معرفة أحوال الأشياء بقدر الطاقة البشرية على ما هو المراد بالحكمة، وصنعوا الحقائق أنواعاً وأجناساً وغيرها، كالإنسان والحيوان والموجود، وبحثوا عن أحوالها المختصة وأثبتوها لها بالأدلة، فحصلت لهم قضايا كسبية محمولاتها أعراض ذاتية لتلك الحقائق، سموها بالمسائل، وجعلوا كل طائفة منها يرجع إلى واحد من تلك الأشياء، بأن تكون موضوعاتها نفسه أو جزءاً له أو نوعاً منه أو عرضاً ذاتياً له، علماً خاصاً يفرد.
He said: And its subject matter is the things, insofar as establishing them is connected to it. I say: The community agrees that the discrimination of sciences in themselves is only according to the differentiation of subject matters. So it is fitting to preface the science with an exposition of the subject matter, to convey that by which it is discriminated in essence after the definition conveyed discrimination in concept. Also, to know the aspect of unity for the multiplicity sought, achieving an encompassing grasp of it in summary, so that when one intends to obtain its details, the seeker does not turn away from what is part of it to what is not part of it. There is no doubt that the aspect of unity of the questions (مسائل) of a science, primarily and essentially, is the subject matter, for in it they share and by it they are united, as we will detail. The reality of the matter is that when they attempted to know the states of things to the extent of human capacity, as is meant by wisdom (الحكمة), and they arranged realities into species and genera and so on, such as human, animal, and existent, and they investigated their specific states and proved them for them by proofs, there resulted for them acquired propositions whose predicates are essential accidents (أعراض ذاتية) for those realities; they called them questions (مسائل). And they made each group of them refer back to one of those things, such that their subject matters are itself, or a part of it, or a species of it, or an essential accident of it, as a special science distinguished.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage discusses the subject matter (موضوع) of ilm al-kalam. The author first quotes the matn: 'Its subject matter is the things, insofar as establishing them is connected to it.' Then he comments ('I say') that scholars agree sciences are distinguished by their subject matters. Thus it is appropriate to begin a science by stating its subject matter, which gives the science its identity in essence (after the definition gave it conceptual identity). Moreover, knowing the subject provides a unifying aspect for the many questions of the science, enabling the student to have a holistic overview and not stray into unrelated topics. The author insists that the primary unifying factor of a science's questions is its subject matter, as questions share that subject and are united by it. He then provides a historical-epistemological explanation: scholars, in their pursuit of wisdom (الحكمة), investigated the states of things, classified realities into genera and species, and derived acquired propositions whose predicates are essential accidents (أعراض ذاتية) of those realities. These propositions are called questions (مسائل). They then grouped these questions under a single subject, which could be the subject itself, a part of it, a species of it, or an essential accident of it, thereby forming a distinct science. This explains how the subject matter of kalam—the things insofar as they relate to establishing beliefs—unifies its questions.

حكمة
مسائل

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the questions of kalam are arbitrary or unrelated to its subject matter.
Correction: They are systematically derived from the study of realities as essential accidents of the subject.

Checkpoint
What are the predicates of the acquired propositions that scholars called 'masa'il'?
A) Accidental properties
B) Essential accidents
C) Necessary attributes
D) Logical categories

Key Takeaway
The questions of kalam are acquired propositions whose predicates are essential accidents of the subject matter, systematically derived from the study of realities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The scholars derived their questions systematically from realities. Are your own beliefs about God and existence based on a similar rigorous investigation, or have you accepted them without proof? What specific step can you take today to examine one foundational belief with the same care these scholars showed?
?
They classified realities into species and genera to study their states. In your daily life, do you take the time to understand the true nature of the things you rely on—your faith, your practices, your relationships—or do you act on vague assumptions? Which 'reality' in your life would benefit most from such classification, and what would that look like?
?
The questions of kalam are not arbitrary; they are proven and essential. Are there any areas of your faith where you hold opinions without evidence, following only tradition or emotion? Will you commit to seeking proof for at least one such area starting today, even if it challenges your comfort?

What Is Kalam?

The Subject of Kalam: Al-Ma'lum
Al-Taftazani defines the subject of kalam as al-ma'lum and explains its scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Taftazani defines the subject of kalam as al-ma'lum (the known) rather than al-mawjud (the existent), and what this definition includes.

Core Idea
The subject of kalam is everything that can be known insofar as it relates to Islamic creed.

Al-Taftazani begins his discussion of the science of kalam by defining its subject matter. This is a crucial step because the subject determines the scope of the discipline. In this passage, he carefully selects the term 'al-ma'lum' (the known) over other candidates, and explains what falls under it. Understanding this choice reveals how kalam relates to other Islamic sciences and what kinds of questions it addresses.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage aloud
Read the Arabic text once to get a feel for its rhythm and structure. Note the key terms: al-ma'lum, al-mawjud, al-'aqa'id al-diniyyah.
2
Identify the main claim
What is al-Taftazani's definition of the subject of kalam? Notice he says it is al-ma'lum insofar as religious doctrines relate to it.
3
Contrast al-ma'lum with al-mawjud
Why does he prefer al-ma'lum over al-mawjud? Think about what al-ma'lum includes that al-mawjud does not, especially mental existence.
4
Explore the scope of kalam
The passage lists states of the Creator and states of bodies/accidents. Note that these constitute Islamic creed or are means to it. This shows the comprehensive nature of kalam.
5
Consider the footnotes
Read the footnotes, especially the explanation of al-ma'lum and the definition of the subject of an art. They clarify key concepts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موضوع علم الكلام هو المعلوم من حيث يتعلق به إثبات العقائد الدينية لما أنه يبحث عن أحوال الصانع من القدم والوحدة والقدرة والإرادة وغيرها، وأحوال الجسم والعرض من الحدوث والافتقار والتركب من الأجزاء وقبول الفناء ونحو ذلك مما هو عقيدة إسلامية أو وسيلة إليها، وكل هذا بحث عن أحوال المعلوم وهو كالموجود بين الهلية والشمول الموضوعات سائر العلوم الإسلامية، فيكون الكلام فوق الكل إلا أنه أوثر على الموجود ليصح على رأي من يقول بالموجود الذهني، ولا يفسر العلم بحصول الصورة في العقل ويرى مباحث المعدوم والحال من مسائل الكلام.
الهامش:
(1) موضوع الفن هو ما يبحث فيه عن عوارضه الذاتية أو ما إليها فيبحث فيه عن الموجود من حيث إنه قديم أو حادث مثلاً وعن المعدوم من حيث إنه ممكن، وعن الحال من حيث حدوثه أو قدمه، ومن حيث تحقيق الدليل على كونه رتبة بين الوجود والعدم.
(2) المعلوم أي ما يدرك ويتصور في الجملة لأنه هو الذي يعم الموجود والمعدوم والحال.
(3) ما بين القوسين سقط من (ب).
(4) في (ب) الوجود.
The subject of the science of kalam is the known (al-ma'lum) insofar as establishing religious doctrines is related to it, because it investigates the states of the Maker (al-Sani') as to eternity (al-qidam), oneness (al-wahdah), power (al-qudrah), will (al-iradah) and others, and the states of body (al-jism) and accident (al-'arad) as to temporality (al-huduth), need (al-iftiqar), composition from parts (al-tarkub min al-ajza'), susceptibility to annihilation (qabul al-fana') and the like, all of which is Islamic creed (aqidah islamiyyah) or a means to it. And all this is an investigation of the states of the known (al-ma'lum), and it is like the existent (al-mawjud) in terms of universality and comprehensiveness over the subjects of the rest of the Islamic sciences. Thus kalam is above all, except that it was preferred over the existent to be correct according to the view of those who affirm mental existence (al-wujud al-dhihni). And the science is not interpreted as the acquisition of the form in the intellect, and he holds that the investigations of the non-existent (al-ma'dum) and the state (al-hal) are among the issues of kalam.
Footnote (1): The subject of the art is that in which is investigated its essential accidents ('awaridh dhatiyyah) or what pertains to them. So in it is investigated the existent insofar as it is eternal or temporal, for example, and the non-existent insofar as it is possible, and the state insofar as it is temporal or eternal, and insofar as verifying the proof that it is a rank between existence and non-existence.
Footnote (2): The known: that is, whatever is perceived and conceptualized in general, because it is what encompasses the existent, the non-existent, and the state.
Footnote (3): What is between the brackets is omitted from (B).
Footnote (4): In (B): 'al-wujud' (the existent).
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage defines the subject matter of the science of kalam. Al-Taftazani states that the subject is 'al-ma'lum' (the known), specifically as it relates to establishing religious doctrines (al-'aqa'id al-diniyyah). He explains that kalam investigates the states of the Creator (al-Sani') such as eternity, oneness, power, and will, as well as the states of bodies and accidents such as temporality, need, composition, and annihilation. These topics constitute Islamic creed or are means to it. All of this is an investigation of the states of the known, and the known is like the existent in its universality over the subjects of other Islamic sciences, making kalam superior to them. He then addresses a nuance: although the subject could be said to be 'al-mawjud' (the existent), al-Taftazani notes that 'al-ma'lum' is preferred because it allows for the inclusion of mental existence (al-wujud al-dhihni), which is necessary for those who affirm it. He also clarifies that the term 'ilm (science) is not defined as the acquisition of a form in the intellect, and that investigations of the non-existent (al-ma'dum) and the state (al-hal) are considered part of kalam. The footnotes further elaborate: the first defines the subject of an art as that which investigates its essential accidents; the second explains that 'al-ma'lum' encompasses whatever is perceived; the third notes a textual variant; and the fourth notes a variant reading of 'al-mawjud'.

C) Because it excludes the non-existent.
D) Because it is the term used in all other Islamic sciences.

Key Takeaway
Al-Taftazani defines the subject of kalam as al-ma'lum (the known) to encompass all that can be known and related to Islamic creed, including the Creator, bodies, accidents, the non-existent, and the state.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How does the realization that kalam studies everything knowable for the sake of creed—including your own existence and the existence of the Creator—change the way you approach your daily thoughts about God and the world? Will you now intentionally reflect on the 'known' around you as a means to strengthen your faith?
?
Al-Taftazani argues that the subject of kalam is al-ma'lum rather than al-mawjud to include mental existence. Are you content to limit your understanding of faith to what is physically tangible, or will you strive to also know the realities that are known only through the intellect and revelation? What step will you take today to expand your 'known' of Islamic creed?
?
The passage explicitly includes the non-existent and the state as part of kalam's subject. How does this challenge your assumption that faith deals only with what is present and tangible? In what area of your life have you neglected to consider the unseen or the possible in light of your belief in God?

The Subject of Ilm al-Kalam: The Knowable
The author defines the subject of kalam as the knowable and presents an objection about the generality of predicates.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the subject of ilm al-kalam is defined as the knowable (al-ma'lum) and how it encompasses the existent, non-existent, and states.

Core Idea
The knowable is the most inclusive subject for kalam, covering all entities relevant to creed.

The author begins by stating the subject of kalam is the knowable. He explains that kalam investigates the attributes of the Creator and creation, all of which are states of the knowable. He then addresses a potential objection: the predicates discussed are either more specific or more general than the subject, which sets up the need for a deeper discussion of essential accidents.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the definition and the objection.
2
Identify the definition
Locate the sentence where the author states the subject of kalam. What is it?
It is 'al-ma'lum' (the knowable).
3
Understand the preference for the knowable
The author says the knowable is preferred over the existent. Why? Because it includes mental existents and non-existents.
4
Analyze the objection
The objection states that if the subject is the concept of knowable, predicates are more specific; if the referent, predicates are more general. Neither seems suitable.
This objection challenges the definition.
5
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this objection matters for the coherence of the science. The next lesson will provide the resolution.
This lesson ends with the problem unsolved.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
موضوع (۱) علم الكلام
موضوع علم الكلام هو المعلوم (۲) من حيث يتعلق به إثبات العقائد الدينية لما أنه يبحث عن أحوال الصانع من القدم والوحدة والقدرة، والإرادة وغيرها، وأحوال الجسم والعرض من الحدوث، والافتقار والتركب من الأجزاء، وقبول الفناء ونحو ذلك مما هو عقيدة إسلامية، أو وسيلة إليها، وكل هذا بحث عن
أحوال :
المعلوم وهو كالموجود بين الهلية والشمول الموضوعات سائر (۳) العلوم الإسلامية، فيكون الكلام فوق الكل [إلا أنه أوثر على الموجود ليصح على رأي
من يقول بالموجود ] (٤) الذهني، ولا يفسر العلم بحصول الصورة في العقل ویری مباحث المعدوم والحال من مسائل الكلام فإن قيل : إن أريد بالمعلوم أو الموجود مفهومه، فكثير من محمولات المسائل بل أكثرها أخص منه وهو ظاهر، وإن أريد معروضه فأعم كرؤية الصانع وقدم كلامه، وحدوث الجسم ونحو ذلك، ولا خلاف في أن الأخص لا يكون عرضاً ذاتياً، والأعم لا يستعمل على عمومه
يرجع
(۱) موضوع الفن هو ما يبحث فيه عن عوارضه الذاتية أو ما إليها فيبحث فيه عن الموجود من حيث إنه قديم أو حادث مثلاً وعن المعدوم من حيث إنه ممكن، وعن الحال من حيث حدوثه أو قدمه، ومن حيث تحقيق الدليل على كونه رتبة بين الوجود والعدم . (۲) المعلوم أي ما يدرك ويتصور في الجملة لأنه هو الذي يعم الموجود والمعدوم . والحال . (۳) ما بين القوسين سقط من (ب).
(٤) في (ب) الوجود .
كالمساواة العارضة للعدد بواسطة الكم لا يستعمل في الحساب إلا بعد التخصيص بالمساواة العددية، وإنما الخلاف في أنه قبل التخصيص، هل يسمى عرضاً ذاتياً
أم لا ..؟
قلنا لزوم الاختصاص ليس بالنظر إلى موضوع المسألة، بل موضوع العلم أعم من أن يكون على الإطلاق أو التقابل كالعدد لا يخلو عن الزوجية، والفردية (1) ألا يرى أن الزوج يحمل على مضروب الفرد في الزوج مع كونه أعم منه. قال في الشفاء : العرض الذاتي قد يكون مساوياً للموضوع، كمساواة الزوايا(۲) الثلاث للقائمتين للمثلث ، وقد يكون أخص منه مطلقاً كالزوج للعدد أو من وجه كالمساواة للعدد فإنها عرض ذاتي له لكون جنسه وهو الكم مأخوذاً في حدها ثم إنهما قد يوجدان معاً، وقد يوجد العدد بدونها وهو ظاهر، وبالعكس كما في المقادير وقد يكون أعم منه مطلقاً كالزوج لمضروب الفرد في الزوج.
Subject (1) of the science of kalam: The subject of the science of kalam is the knowable (al-ma'lum) (2) insofar as it pertains to the establishment of religious beliefs, because it investigates the states of the Maker — such as eternality, unity, power, will, and others — and the states of the body and accident — such as origination, contingency, composition from parts, susceptibility to annihilation, and the like — which are Islamic creed or means to it. All of this is an investigation of the states of the knowable, which is like the existent (al-mawjud) in terms of encompassing the subjects of the other (3) Islamic sciences, so kalam is above all. [But the knowable is preferred over the existent to be valid according to the opinion of one who affirms the mental existent] (4), and the science is not explained as the acquisition of a form in the intellect, and one sees that the investigations of the non-existent and the state are from the issues of kalam. For if it is said: if the intended meaning by 'the knowable' or 'the existent' is its concept, then many of the predicates of the issues — indeed most of them — are more specific than it, and this is obvious; and if the intended meaning is its referent, then it is more general, such as the vision of the Maker, the eternality of His speech, the origination of the body, and the like. There is no disagreement that the more specific is not an essential accident, and the more general is not used in its full generality. (1) The subject of an art is that which is investigated in terms of its essential accidents or what pertains to them; thus, it investigates the existent insofar as it is eternal or originated, for example, and the non-existent insofar as it is possible, and the state insofar as its origination or eternality, and insofar as establishing the proof that it is a rank between existence and non-existence. (2) The knowable: that which is perceived and conceptualized in general, because it is that which includes the existent, the non-existent, and the state. (3) What is between the brackets is omitted from copy (b). (4) In copy (b): 'al-wujud' (existence). It is like equality, which is accidental to number through quantity, but not used in arithmetic except after specification by numerical equality; the disagreement is only whether before specification it is called an essential accident or not. We said: the necessity of specificity is not with respect to the subject of the issue; rather, the subject of the science is more general absolutely or in terms of opposition, like number which is not free from evenness and oddness (1). Do you not see that 'even' is predicated of the product of an odd number and an even number, even though it is more general than it? He said in al-Shifa: The essential accident can be equal to the subject, like the equality of the three (2) angles to two right angles for the triangle; and it can be more specific absolutely, like 'even' for number; or in some respect, like equality for number, for it is an essential accident for it because its genus — which is quantity — is taken in its definition; then the two may exist together, and number may exist without it — this is obvious — and conversely, as in magnitudes; and it can be more general absolutely, like 'even' for the product of an odd number and an even number.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage is a definition and defense of the subject matter of ilm al-kalam. The author begins by stating that the subject is the knowable (al-ma'lum) insofar as it relates to establishing religious beliefs. He explains that kalam investigates the attributes of the Creator (such as eternality, unity, power, will) and the attributes of bodies and accidents (such as origination, contingency, composition, annihilation). All of these are states of the knowable. The author then addresses a potential objection: if the subject is the knowable or the existent, the predicates (e.g., 'eternal') are either more specific (if the subject is the concept) or more general (if the subject is the referent). He responds by discussing essential accidents ('arad dhati), citing Avicenna's al-Shifa. The key point is that an essential accident need not be coextensive with its subject; it can be equal, more specific, or more general. Thus, the subject of kalam can be broader than its predicates, and this is acceptable. The author uses mathematical examples (number, evenness, equality) to illustrate this logical point. The passage also includes footnotes clarifying terms and variant readings.

Key Terms
المعلوم
الموجود
العرض الذاتي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The subject of a science must be exactly coextensive with all its predicates.
Correction: The passage shows that this is not required; the subject can be broader and essential accidents can be more specific or more general.

Checkpoint
What is the subject of ilm al-kalam according to the passage?
A) The existent (al-mawjud)
B) The knowable (al-ma'lum)
C) The religious beliefs themselves
D) The Creator

Key Takeaway
The subject of kalam is the knowable, which includes the existent, non-existent, and states, even though some predicates are more specific or more general.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author selects 'the knowable' as the subject of kalam to include non-existent and states. Is there a 'knowable' truth about your own spiritual state (like a hidden sin or a neglected obligation) that you avoid because it doesn't fit your comfortable category of 'existent'? Will you deliberately examine it today?
?
If the subject of a science must be exactly coextensive with its predicates, then kalam's subject seems flawed. How does this tension affect your trust in the method of kalam? Are you willing to accept a subject that is not perfectly coextensive, or does this challenge your assumptions about certainty in theology?

Essential Accidents and the Solution to Generality
The author resolves the objection by explaining the types of essential accidents, citing Avicenna.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the concept of essential accidents resolves the objection that the subject of kalam is too broad or too narrow.

Core Idea
Essential accidents can be equal, more specific, or more general than their subject, so the subject can be broad.

The author responds to the objection by clarifying that the requirement for an essential accident does not demand coextension. Using examples from number and geometry, he shows that essential accidents can be equal, more specific, or more general. This validates the choice of the knowable as subject.

Guided Path
1
Read the response passage
Read the Arabic and translation of the response. Note the main claim.
2
Understand the main claim
The author says the necessity of specificity is not with respect to the subject of the issue but the subject of the science can be more general.
This is the core resolution.
3
Analyze the number example
Number is the subject; evenness is an essential accident even though it is more specific. The author explains why.
The genus (quantity) is involved in the definition of evenness.
4
Study Avicenna's classification
Identify the three types of essential accidents: equal, more specific (absolutely or partially), more general.
These are from al-Shifa.
5
Relate back to the knowable
The knowable can be the subject even if its predicates are not coextensive, because essential accidents need not be coextensive.

Source Text
