موضوع (۱) علم الكلام
موضوع علم الكلام هو المعلوم (۲) من حيث يتعلق به إثبات العقائد الدينية لما أنه يبحث عن أحوال الصانع من القدم والوحدة والقدرة، والإرادة وغيرها، وأحوال الجسم والعرض من الحدوث، والافتقار والتركب من الأجزاء، وقبول الفناء ونحو ذلك مما هو عقيدة إسلامية، أو وسيلة إليها، وكل هذا بحث عن
أحوال :
المعلوم وهو كالموجود بين الهلية والشمول الموضوعات سائر (۳) العلوم الإسلامية، فيكون الكلام فوق الكل [إلا أنه أوثر على الموجود ليصح على رأي
من يقول بالموجود ] (٤) الذهني، ولا يفسر العلم بحصول الصورة في العقل ویری مباحث المعدوم والحال من مسائل الكلام فإن قيل : إن أريد بالمعلوم أو الموجود مفهومه، فكثير من محمولات المسائل بل أكثرها أخص منه وهو ظاهر، وإن أريد معروضه فأعم كرؤية الصانع وقدم كلامه، وحدوث الجسم ونحو ذلك، ولا خلاف في أن الأخص لا يكون عرضاً ذاتياً، والأعم لا يستعمل على عمومه
يرجع
(۱) موضوع الفن هو ما يبحث فيه عن عوارضه الذاتية أو ما إليها فيبحث فيه عن الموجود من حيث إنه قديم أو حادث مثلاً وعن المعدوم من حيث إنه ممكن، وعن الحال من حيث حدوثه أو قدمه، ومن حيث تحقيق الدليل على كونه رتبة بين الوجود والعدم . (۲) المعلوم أي ما يدرك ويتصور في الجملة لأنه هو الذي يعم الموجود والمعدوم . والحال . (۳) ما بين القوسين سقط من (ب).

كالمساواة العارضة للعدد بواسطة الكم لا يستعمل في الحساب إلا بعد التخصيص بالمساواة العددية، وإنما الخلاف في أنه قبل التخصيص، هل يسمى عرضاً ذاتياً

قلنا لزوم الاختصاص ليس بالنظر إلى موضوع المسألة، بل موضوع العلم أعم من أن يكون على الإطلاق أو التقابل كالعدد لا يخلو عن الزوجية، والفردية (1) ألا يرى أن الزوج يحمل على مضروب الفرد في الزوج مع كونه أعم منه. قال في الشفاء : العرض الذاتي قد يكون مساوياً للموضوع، كمساواة الزوايا(۲) الثلاث للقائمتين للمثلث ، وقد يكون أخص منه مطلقاً كالزوج للعدد أو من وجه كالمساواة للعدد فإنها عرض ذاتي له لكون جنسه وهو الكم مأخوذاً في حدها ثم إنهما قد يوجدان معاً، وقد يوجد العدد بدونها وهو ظاهر، وبالعكس كما في المقادير وقد يكون أعم منه مطلقاً كالزوج لمضروب الفرد في الزوج.
Subject (1) of the science of kalam: The subject of the science of kalam is the knowable (al-ma'lum) (2) insofar as it pertains to the establishment of religious beliefs, because it investigates the states of the Maker — such as eternality, unity, power, will, and others — and the states of the body and accident — such as origination, contingency, composition from parts, susceptibility to annihilation, and the like — which are Islamic creed or means to it. All of this is an investigation of the states of the knowable, which is like the existent (al-mawjud) in terms of encompassing the subjects of the other (3) Islamic sciences, so kalam is above all. [But the knowable is preferred over the existent to be valid according to the opinion of one who affirms the mental existent] (4), and the science is not explained as the acquisition of a form in the intellect, and one sees that the investigations of the non-existent and the state are from the issues of kalam. For if it is said: if the intended meaning by 'the knowable' or 'the existent' is its concept, then many of the predicates of the issues — indeed most of them — are more specific than it, and this is obvious; and if the intended meaning is its referent, then it is more general, such as the vision of the Maker, the eternality of His speech, the origination of the body, and the like. There is no disagreement that the more specific is not an essential accident, and the more general is not used in its full generality. (1) The subject of an art is that which is investigated in terms of its essential accidents or what pertains to them; thus, it investigates the existent insofar as it is eternal or originated, for example, and the non-existent insofar as it is possible, and the state insofar as its origination or eternality, and insofar as establishing the proof that it is a rank between existence and non-existence. (2) The knowable: that which is perceived and conceptualized in general, because it is that which includes the existent, the non-existent, and the state. (3) What is between the brackets is omitted from copy (b). (4) In copy (b): 'al-wujud' (existence). It is like equality, which is accidental to number through quantity, but not used in arithmetic except after specification by numerical equality; the disagreement is only whether before specification it is called an essential accident or not. We said: the necessity of specificity is not with respect to the subject of the issue; rather, the subject of the science is more general absolutely or in terms of opposition, like number which is not free from evenness and oddness (1). Do you not see that 'even' is predicated of the product of an odd number and an even number, even though it is more general than it? He said in al-Shifa: The essential accident can be equal to the subject, like the equality of the three (2) angles to two right angles for the triangle; and it can be more specific absolutely, like 'even' for number; or in some respect, like equality for number, for it is an essential accident for it because its genus — which is quantity — is taken in its definition; then the two may exist together, and number may exist without it — this is obvious — and conversely, as in magnitudes; and it can be more general absolutely, like 'even' for the product of an odd number and an even number.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage is a definition and defense of the subject matter of ilm al-kalam. The author begins by stating that the subject is the knowable (al-ma'lum) insofar as it relates to establishing religious beliefs. He explains that kalam investigates the attributes of the Creator (such as eternality, unity, power, will) and the attributes of bodies and accidents (such as origination, contingency, composition, annihilation). All of these are states of the knowable. The author then addresses a potential objection: if the subject is the knowable or the existent, the predicates (e.g., 'eternal') are either more specific (if the subject is the concept) or more general (if the subject is the referent). He responds by discussing essential accidents ('arad dhati), citing Avicenna's al-Shifa. The key point is that an essential accident need not be coextensive with its subject; it can be equal, more specific, or more general. Thus, the subject of kalam can be broader than its predicates, and this is acceptable. The author uses mathematical examples (number, evenness, equality) to illustrate this logical point. The passage also includes footnotes clarifying terms and variant readings.

المساواة
الزوجية
العدد
المثلث

Checkpoint
According to the passage from al-Shifa, which of the following is NOT a type of essential accident?
A) Equal to the subject
B) More specific than the subject
C) More general than the subject
D) Completely unrelated to the subject

Key Takeaway
Essential accidents can be equal, more specific, or more general than their subject, so the subject of kalam can be as broad as the knowable.

What Is Kalam?

Definition of the Issues (Masā'il) of Kalam
The author defines the issues of kalam as theoretical religious propositions sought through demonstration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what constitutes an 'issue' (mas'ala) in kalam and why self-evident propositions are not counted among the issues of a science.

Core Idea
An issue in kalam is a theoretical religious proposition sought through proof, not a self-evident truth.

In this passage, the author clarifies the technical meaning of 'issues' (masā'il) in the science of kalam. He distinguishes between theoretical propositions, which require proof, and self-evident truths, which do not. He also notes that even self-evident propositions can become 'issues' when we seek to explain why they are self-evident. This distinction is foundational for understanding how kalam proceeds as a demonstrative discipline.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the key terms: مسائل, قضايا, بديهي. Pay attention to the definition of 'issue' as something asked about and sought through proof.
The author emphasizes that there is no disagreement about self-evident not being issues.
2
Identify the three qualifications
The author says issues are 'theoretical religious creedal propositions'. Understand why 'theoretical' is crucial, and why self-evident matters are excluded.
Self-evident matters can be included only to explain why they are self-evident; then they become acquired (kasbī).
3
Connect to the logic reference
The author interprets the statement from Tajrīd al-Manṭiq that issues are what is proved in a science if not evident, consistent with the given definition.
This shows the definition applies across sciences, not just kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسائل علم الكلام
قال : مسائلة القضايا (۳) النظرية الشرعية الاعتقادية
أقول : قد يجعل من مقدمات العلم تصور مسائله إجمالاً لإفادته زيادة التميز وقيد القضايا بالنظرية لأنه لم يقع خلاف في أن البديهي لا يكون من المسائل، والمطالب العملية، بل لا معنى (٤) للمسألة إلا ما يسأل عنه، ويطلب بالدليل نعم قد يورد في المسائل الحكم البديهي ليتبين لميته وهو من هذه الحثيثية كسبي لا بديهي لا بديهي (٥) وقد تجعل الصناعة عبارة عن عدة أوضاع واصطلاحات وأحكام بينة تفتقر إلى تنبيه (٦) هي مسائلها، وعلى هذا ينبغي أن يحمل ما وقع في تجريد المنطق من أن المسائل ما يبرهن عليها في العلم إن لم تكن بينة .
(۱) في (أ) ألا يرى.
(۳) القضايا : جمع قضية هي ما اشتمل من المعاني الكلامية على إثبات أو سلب تامين بحيث السكوت يحصل على اللفظ الدال عليها .
(۲) سقط من (ب) الثلاث.
(٤) في (ب) العلمية وهو تحريف .
(٥) في (ب) ليتبين لميته وهو من هذه الحيثية كسبي لا بديهي .
(٦) في (ب) تنبه
Issues (masā'il) of the science of kalam. He said: His issues are the theoretical religious propositions (al-qadāyā al-naẓariyya al-shar'iyya al-i'tiqādiyya) (3). I say: It may be made from the premises of the science a general mental conception of its issues, for it gives additional distinction. And the qualification 'theoretical' is because there is no disagreement that the self-evident (al-badīhī) is not from the issues, nor are practical demands. Rather, there is no meaning (4) of 'issue' except what is asked about and sought through proof. Indeed, a self-evident judgment may be brought into the issues to clarify the reason for its self-evidence, and it is from this respect acquired (kasbī), not self-evident (5). And the art (al-ṣinā'a) may be made to consist of several positions, technical terms, and evident rulings that need a reminder (6); these are its issues. And accordingly, one should interpret what occurs in Tajrīd al-Manṭiq that 'the issues are that which is proved in the science if they are not evident.' (1) In copy (a): 'alā yarā' (do you not see). (3) Al-qadāyā: plural of qadiyya, which is that which comprises of kalamic meanings a complete affirmation or negation such that silence is obtained upon the wording that indicates them. (2) 'Three' is omitted from copy (b). (4) In copy (b): 'al-'ilmiyya' (scientific), which is a corruption. (5) In copy (b): 'liyutabayyina limiyyatahu wa huwa min hādhihi al-ḥaythiyya kasbī lā badīhī' (to clarify why it is self-evident, and it is from this respect acquired, not self-evident). (6) In copy (b): 'tanabbuh' (attention).
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage defines what is meant by 'issues' (masā'il) in the science of kalam. The author begins by citing a source that says the issues are theoretical religious propositions (al-qadāyā al-naẓariyya al-shar'iyya al-i'tiqādiyya). He then explains that the qualification 'theoretical' is important because self-evident (badīhī) propositions are not considered issues, nor are practical matters. An issue is that which is asked about and sought through proof (dalīl). However, a self-evident judgment may be included in the issues in order to explain the reason for its self-evidence, and in that respect it becomes acquired (kasbī) rather than self-evident. The author also notes that an art (ṣinā'a) may consist of several positions, technical terms, and evident rulings that require a reminder; these are its issues. Finally, he refers to the Tajrīd al-Manṭiq and says that its statement — that the issues are what is proved in a science if they are not evident — should be interpreted in this light. The footnotes provide variant readings and clarify the definition of 'qadiyya' (proposition).

The Problems of Kalam: Theoretical Propositions
Sanusi defines the problems of kalam and their essential characteristics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the problems (masa'il) of kalam are exclusively theoretical (nazariyya) religious faith-based propositions that require proof, and you will grasp the nuances regarding intuitive and practical matters.

Core Idea
Kalam problems are only theoretical matters that need proof, not intuitive or practical.

Sanusi begins by defining what constitutes a problem in kalam. He clarifies that only theoretical propositions—those requiring rational proof—qualify, excluding intuitive truths and practical matters. However, he notes an important nuance: sometimes intuitive judgments are included when seeking their rational cause, making them acquired from that perspective. This lesson unpacks that definition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the key terms and the structure of the definition.
Pay attention to the phrase 'القضايا النظرية الشرعية الاعتقادية'.
2
Identify the core definition
The author states that the problems are 'theoretical legal faith-based propositions'. Note the three qualifiers: theoretical, legal (shar'iyya), faith-based (i'tiqadiyya).
3
Understand why 'theoretical' is important
The qualifier 'theoretical' excludes two things: intuitive propositions and practical demands. The text says there is no disagreement that intuitive (badihi) is not among the problems.
Intuitive propositions are self-evident and need no proof.
4
Examine the exception
An intuitive judgment can be brought into the problems to clarify its reason (limiyya). From that angle, it becomes acquired (kasbi), not intuitive. This nuance shows flexibility.
This relates to the concept of 'limiyya' (why something is the case).
5
Connect to the broader tradition
The author aligns his definition with that in Tajrid al-Mantiq: problems are what are proven in the science if they are not evident. This shows the consistency of the definition across disciplines.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسائل علم الكلام قال : مسائلة القضايا النظرية الشرعية الاعتقادية أقول : قد يجعل من مقدمات العلم تصور مسائله إجمالاً لإفادته زيادة التميز وقيد القضايا بالنظرية لأنه لم يقع خلاف في أن البديهي لا يكون من المسائل، والمطالب العملية، بل لا معنى للمسألة إلا ما يسأل عنه، ويطلب بالدليل نعم قد يورد في المسائل الحكم البديهي ليتبين لميته وهو من هذه الحثيثية كسبي لا بديهي لا بديهي وقد تجعل الصناعة عبارة عن عدة أوضاع واصطلاحات وأحكام بينة تفتقر إلى تنبيه هي مسائلها، وعلى هذا ينبغي أن يحمل ما وقع في تجريد المنطق من أن المسائل ما يبرهن عليها في العلم إن لم تكن بينة .
Problems of the Science of Kalam. He said: Its problems are theoretical legal faith-based propositions. I say: From the premises of a science, one may form an overall conception of its problems to provide additional distinction. The qualification 'theoretical' (nazariyya) is because there is no disagreement that the intuitive (badihi) is not among the problems, nor are practical demands. Rather, the meaning of 'problem' (mas'ala) is nothing but that which is asked about and sought by proof. Yes, an intuitive judgment may be brought into the problems to clarify its reason (limiyya), and from this aspect it is acquired (kasbi), not intuitive. And the art (sina'a) may be made an expression of several postures, terminologies, and evident rulings that need indication; these are its problems. And upon this should be understood what occurs in Tajrid al-Mantiq that problems are what are proven in the science if they are not evident.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage defines the problems (masa'il) of the science of kalam. The author states that the problems are theoretical (nazariyya) religious faith-based propositions. He explains that the qualifier 'theoretical' is crucial because there is consensus that intuitive (badihi) propositions are not considered problems of a science; similarly, practical matters are excluded. A problem is essentially something that needs to be sought and established through proof. However, the author notes an exception: sometimes an intuitive judgment is included as a problem for the purpose of demonstrating its rational cause (limiyya). In that context, the judgment becomes acquired (kasbi) from this perspective, not intuitive. The author then discusses the term 'sina'a' (art) which can be understood as a set of established positions, terminologies, and self-evident rulings that require elucidation; these form the problems. He concludes by aligning this with the definition in Tajrid al-Mantiq: problems are those things that are proven within a science if they are not already evident.

القضايا النظرية
البديهي

Misconception: Any question about religion is a problem of kalam.
Correction: Only theoretical propositions that require rational proof are problems; intuitive or practical matters are excluded.

Key Takeaway
The problems of kalam are exclusively theoretical religious faith-based propositions that are sought by proof.

The Goal and Benefit of Kalam
The author defines the goal and benefit of kalam with terminological distinctions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the science of kalam has both a worldly and an afterlife benefit, and how its goal of adorning faith with certainty protects against doubts.

Core Idea
Kalam: This-worldly order + Next-worldly salvation.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies what makes a science worth pursuing. He shows that kalam aims to make faith certain and firm, yielding benefits both in society and in the afterlife. This lesson unpacks those terms and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp the flow.
Notice the distinction between ghaya (goal) and manfa'a (benefit).
2
Distinguish key terms
Identify the definitions of ghaya, gharad, and manfa'a as the commentator explains them.
Ghaya: what a thing leads to; gharad: what is sought; manfa'a: universally desired.
3
Identify the goal and benefits of kalam
Find the specific goal (making faith certain) and the two benefits (worldly order and afterlife salvation) stated at the end.
The worldly benefit involves justice and social order; the afterlife benefit is salvation from punishment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غاية علم الكلام (قال): وغايته تحلية الإيمان بالإيقان ومنفعته الفوز بنظام المعاش ونجاة المعاد) أقول : ما يتأدى إليه الشيء ويترتب عليه يسمى من هذه الحيثية غاية، ومن حيث يطلب للفعل غرضاً ، ثم إن كان مما يتشوقه الكل طبعاً يسمى منفعة فيصدر العلم يذكر غايته ليعلم أنه هل يوافق غرضه أم لا ...؟ ولئلا يكون نظره عبثاً أو ضلالاً ومنفعته ليزداد طالبه جداً ونشاطاً. وغاية الكلام أن يصير الإيمان، والتصديق بالأحكام الشرعية متيقناً محكماً لا تزلزله شبه المبطلين ومنفعته في الدنيا انتظام أمر المعاش بالمحافظة على العدل والمعاملة التي يحتاج إليها في بقاء النوع على وجه لا يؤدي إلى الفساد وفي الآخرة النجاة من العذاب المرتب على الكفر وسوء الاعتقاد .
The Goal of the Science of Kalam. (He said): Its goal is adorning faith with certainty (al-iman bi al-iqan) and its benefit is achieving orderly livelihood and salvation in the afterlife. I say: That which a thing leads to and follows from it is called, from this perspective, a goal (ghaya); and from the perspective that it is sought for an action, it is called an aim (gharad). Then if it is something that everyone naturally desires, it is called a benefit (manfa'a). The science mentions its goal so that one knows whether it agrees with his aim or not, and lest his pursuit be futile or misguided; and its benefit is mentioned so that its seeker increases in seriousness and activity. The goal of kalam is that faith and assent to the legal rulings become certain and firm, not shaken by the doubts of invalidators. Its benefit in this world is the orderly state of livelihood by preserving justice and dealing that is needed for the survival of the species in a way that does not lead to corruption; and in the afterlife, salvation from the punishment attached to disbelief and wrong belief.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage explains the goal (ghaya) and benefit (manfa'a) of the science of kalam. The author first quotes the original text: the goal is to adorn faith with certainty, and the benefit is achieving orderly livelihood (in the dunya) and salvation in the afterlife. He then provides a terminological clarification: what a thing leads to is called a goal (ghaya) from that perspective; from the perspective of being sought for an action, it is called an aim (gharad). If that thing is universally desired by nature, it is called a benefit (manfa'a). The author notes that a science mentions its goal to align with the seeker's purpose and to avoid futility; mentioning the benefit increases the student's diligence. The specific goal of kalam is to make faith (iman) and assent to legal rulings certain (mutayaqqan) and firm (muhkaman), immune to doubts of those who invalidate. The worldly benefit is to maintain a well-ordered society through justice and fair dealings necessary for human survival without corruption. The afterlife benefit is salvation from punishment for disbelief and corrupted beliefs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think kalam only benefits the afterlife, ignoring its worldly benefits.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that kalam also brings worldly benefit: an orderly society through justice and fair dealing.

The Superiority of Kalam over Other Sciences
The author proves that kalam is the most honorable science based on its subject, object, goal, necessity, and certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the criteria that make Kalam the most honorable science and why its subject, goal, and proofs are unparalleled.

Core Idea
Kalam is the most honorable science because of its noble subject, certain proofs, and foundational role.

In this passage, the author establishes the preeminence of Kalam by enumerating the aspects that confer honor upon any science. He shows that Kalam ranks highest in every respect — from its subject matter to the mutual agreement of reason and revelation. This lesson unpacks those criteria and their significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the criteria
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the five aspects mentioned: subject, known thing (object), goal, need, foundation of other sciences, and certainty of proofs.
The passage is compact; each criterion is indicated by a single phrase.
2
Understand why each criterion applies to Kalam
The commentary explains that kalam's subject is God, its goal is eternal salvation, its proofs are certain, etc. Reflect on how each makes it superior.
Consider the contrast with other sciences that deal with lower subjects or less certain proofs.
3
Connect to the broader purpose of Kalam
Consider why the author emphasizes the mutual confirmation of reason and revelation — this is a distinctive feature of kalam that other sciences lack.
This also shows that kalam harmonizes intellectual and revealed knowledge.

Commentary
This passage establishes that kalam is the most honorable of sciences. The author lists the criteria for the honor of a science: its subject matter, its known object (the conclusions it establishes), its goal, the degree of need for it, the dependence of other sciences (especially religious ones) on it, and the certainty and mutual agreement of its proofs (reason and revelation). Since kalam's subject is the highest (God and His attributes), its known thing is the most noble (knowledge of God), its goal is the most honorable (eternal salvation and certainty of faith), other religious sciences depend on it, it is severely needed, and its proofs are certain and agreed upon by reason and revelation, it is proven to be the most honorable. The author adds that this is also supported by reports from the salaf (predecessors), though the passage ends before completing that point.

The Goal and Benefit of Ilm al-Kalam
Author defines the goal and benefit of ilm al-kalam with terminological clarification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the purpose (ghayah) and benefit (manfa'ah) of ilm al-kalam as defined by the author, and why these concepts are essential for the seeker of knowledge.

Core Idea
Ilm al-kalam aims to make faith certain and unshakable, benefiting both worldly life and the hereafter.

Before diving into theological arguments, the author of this text establishes why ilm al-kalam is worth studying. He distinguishes between its goal (what it aims to achieve) and its benefit (what results from it). This passage clarifies that kalam is not mere debate but a tool to solidify faith and ensure a well-ordered life and salvation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the full translation. Let the author's definitions of 'goal' and 'benefit' settle in your mind.
2
Distinguish goal from benefit
Notice how the author first explains the general terms (goal vs. benefit) and then applies them specifically to ilm al-kalam. The goal is internal (certainty of faith), while the benefit has both worldly and otherworldly dimensions.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself why the author emphasizes that the goal is to make faith 'unshakable by doubts'. This frames kalam as a defensive science that protects belief.
The phrase 'لا تزلزله شبه المبطلين' is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غاية علم الكلام
(قال): وغايته تحلية الإيمان بالإيقان ومنفعته الفوز بنظام المعاش ونجاة المعاد)
أقول : ما يتأدى إليه الشيء ويترتب عليه يسمى من هذه الحيثية غاية، ومن حيث يطلب للفعل غرضاً ، ثم إن كان مما يتشوقه الكل طبعاً يسمى منفعة فيصدر العلم يذكر غايته ليعلم أنه هل يوافق غرضه أم لا ...؟ ولئلا يكون نظره عبثاً أو ضلالاً ومنفعته ليزداد طالبه جداً ونشاطاً. وغاية الكلام أن يصير الإيمان، والتصديق بالأحكام الشرعية متيقناً محكماً لا تزلزله شبه المبطلين ومنفعته في الدنيا انتظام أمر المعاش بالمحافظة على العدل والمعاملة التي يحتاج إليها في بقاء النوع على وجه لا يؤدي إلى الفساد وفي الآخرة النجاة من العذاب المرتب على الكفر وسوء الاعتقاد .
The goal of ilm al-kalam. (He said): Its goal is to adorn faith with certainty, and its benefit is success in the order of livelihood and salvation in the hereafter. I say: What something leads to and results from is called from this perspective a goal, and from the perspective that it is sought for the action it is an objective, then if it is something that everyone naturally desires it is called a benefit. Thus the science mentions its goal so that one knows whether it agrees with his objective or not, and so that his consideration is not futile or misguided, and its benefit so that its seeker increases in seriousness and activity. The goal of kalam is that faith and belief in the legal rulings become certain and firm, not shaken by the doubts of the falsifiers, and its benefit in this world is the orderly arrangement of livelihood through preserving justice and the transactions needed for the survival of the species in a way that does not lead to corruption, and in the hereafter salvation from the punishment attached to disbelief and bad belief.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage defines the goal (ghayah) and benefit (manfa'ah) of ilm al-kalam. The author first quotes the matn stating the goal is to adorn faith with certainty (yaqin) and the benefit is success in worldly livelihood and salvation in the hereafter. He then explains the terminology: a goal is what something leads to, and if it is naturally desired by all, it is called a benefit. He notes that a science mentions its goal to ensure alignment with the seeker's objective and to avoid futility. The specific goal of kalam is to make faith in Islamic legal rulings certain and unshakable by doubts. Its worldly benefit is maintaining social order through justice and transactions necessary for human survival without corruption; its otherworldly benefit is salvation from punishment for disbelief and corrupted belief.

What Is Kalam?

The Subject Matter of Kalam: Existent Qua Existent
Author defines subject and method of kalam, citing al-Ghazali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that kalam studies the existent as such, but with a distinct method that separates it from philosophy.

Core Idea
Kalam and philosophy share a subject but diverge in method.

In this passage, the author establishes the foundational definition of kalam: it investigates the existent insofar as it exists. However, this is not a mere repetition of philosophy—the method, as you will see, is grounded in Islamic revelation. The early scholars (al-mutakaddimun) saw the subject as all-encompassing, leading to a systematic analysis that culminates in affirming prophethood and revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the early scholars' view
Begin with the sentence 'The early scholars said that its subject is the existent insofar as it is...' and read through the description of the mutakallim's method. Notice how the investigation proceeds from the most general to the specific.
The passage quotes Imam al-Ghazali to illustrate the method.
2
Identify the divisions made by the mutakallim
The mutakallim divides the existent into eternal and originated, then further divides the originated into substance and accident, and so on. List these divisions as they appear.
3
Understand the endpoint of rational inquiry
After reason demonstrates the necessity of a creator, prophethood, and miracles, the passage states that 'the operation of the intellect ends' and one turns to revelation. This marks the boundary of kalam's rational part.
This shows that kalam is not purely rational but has a revelatory foundation.
4
Distinguish kalam from philosophy
Although both study the existent, kalam is distinguished by its adherence to the law of Islam. The passage later clarifies this, but note here that the method itself is framed by Islamic doctrine.
This point is further elaborated in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطعن فيه، فمحمول على ما إذا قصد التعصب في الدين، وإفساد عقائد المبتدئين، والتوريط في أودية الضلال بتزيين ما للفلسفة المقال. من قال المتقدمون على أن موضوعه الموجود من حيث هو، ويتميز عن الإلهي بكون البحث فيه على قانون الإسلام أي ما علم قطعاً من الدين كصدور الكثرة عن الواحد ونزول الملك من السماء وكون العالم محفوفاً بالعدم والفناء إلى غير ذلك مما تجزم به الملة دون الفلسفة لا ما هو الحق ولو ادعاء لمشاركة الفلسفة ككلام المخالف. أقول: أخر هذه المباحث مع تعلقها بالموضوع محافظة على انتظام الكلام في بيان الموضوع والمسائل والغاية فالمتقدمون من علماء الكلام جعلوا موضوعه الموجود بما هو موجود لرجوع مباحثه إليه على ما قال الإمام حجة الإسلام أن المتكلم ينظر في أعم الأشياء وهو الموجود فيقسمه إلى قديم ومحدث، والمحدث إلى جوهر وعرض والعرض إلى ما يشترط فيه الحياة كالعلم والقدرة وإلى ما لا يشترط كاللون والطعم ويقسم الجوهر إلى الحيوان والنبات والجماد، ويبين أن اختلافها بالأنواع أو بالأعراض، وينظر في القديم فيتبين أنه لا يتكثر ولا يتركب وأنه يتميز عن المحدث بصفات تجب له، وأمور تمتنع عليه، وأحكام تجوز في حقه من غير وجوب أو امتناع، ويبين أن أصل الفعل جائز عليه وأن العالم فعله الجائز فيفتقر بجوازه إلى محدث، وأنه قادر على بعث الرسل وعلى تعريف صدقهم بالمعجزات وأن هذا واقع وحينئذ ينتهي تصرف العقل ويأخذ في التلقي من النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام الثابت عنده صدقه ومقبول ما يقوله في الله تعالى وفي أمر المبدأ والمعاد. ولما كان موضوع العلم الإلهي من الفلسفة هو الموجود بما هو موجود وكان تمايز العلوم بتمايز الموضوعات قيد الموجود ههنا بحيثية كونه متعلقاً للمباحث الجارية على قانون الإسلام، فتميز الكلام عن الإلهي بأن البحث فيه إنما يكون على قانون الإسلام أي الطريقة المعهودة المسماة بالدين والملة، والقواعد المعلومة قطعاً من الكتاب والسنة والإجماع، مثل كون الواحد موجد للكثير، وكون الملك نازلاً من السماء، وكون العالم مسبوقاً بالعدم، وفانياً بعد الوجود، إلى غير ذلك من القواعد التي يقطع بها في الإسلام دون الفلسفة. وإلى هذا أشار من قال: الأصل في هذا العلم التمسك بالكتاب والسنة، أي التعلق بهما وكون مباحثه منتسبة إليهما جارية على قواعدهما على ما هو معنى انتساب العقائد إلى الدين. وقيل المراد بقانون الإسلام أصوله من الكتاب والسنة والإجماع والمعقول الذي لا يخالفها، وبالجملة فحاصله أن يحافظ في جميع المباحث على القواعد الشرعية ولا يخالف القطعيات منها جرياً على مقتضى نظر العقول الفاصرة على ما هو قانون الفلسفة، لا أن يكون جميع المباحث حقة في نفس الأمر منتسبة إلى الإسلام بالتحقيق، وإلا لما صدق التعريف على كلام المجسمة والمعتزلة والخوارج ومن يجري.
Criticism of it, then it is carried upon when one intends fanaticism in religion, corrupting the beliefs of beginners, and involving them in valleys of error by embellishing what belongs to philosophical discourse. The early scholars said that its subject is the existent insofar as it is, and it is distinguished from the divine science (al-ilahi) by the fact that investigation in it is according to the law of Islam (qanun al-Islam), i.e., what is known certainly from religion, such as the emanation of multiplicity from the One, the descent of the angel from heaven, and the world being surrounded by non-existence and annihilation, and other things that the religious community (milla) affirms with certainty, not philosophy — not what is true even if claimed to share with philosophy, like the speech of the opponent. I say: I postponed these discussions despite their connection to the subject to preserve the order of speech in explaining the subject, the issues, and the goal. The early scholars of kalam made its subject the existent qua existent because their investigations refer back to it, as the Imam, the Proof of Islam (al-Ghazali), said: the mutakallim (theologian) looks at the most general of things, which is the existent, and divides it into eternal and originated; the originated into substance and accident; the accident into what requires life, like knowledge and power, and what does not require it, like color and taste; and he divides substance into animal, plant, and inanimate; and he shows that their differences are by species or by accidents. And he looks at the eternal and then it becomes clear that it is not multiple nor composite, and that it is distinguished from the originated by attributes necessarily belonging to it, matters impossible for it, and judgments permissible for it without necessity or impossibility. And he shows that the origin of the action is permissible for Him, and that the world is His permissible action, so by its permissibility it needs an originator; and that He is able to send messengers and to verify their truthfulness by miracles, and that this actually occurs. Then the operation of the intellect ends and one begins to receive from the Prophet (peace be upon him), whose truthfulness is established, and what he says about God Almighty and about the matter of the beginning and the return is accepted. Since the subject of the divine science in philosophy is the existent qua existent, and the differentiation of sciences is by the differentiation of subjects, the existent is here restricted by the respect of its being related to investigations conducted according to the law of Islam. Thus kalam is distinguished from the divine science in that investigation in it is only according to the law of Islam, i.e., the accustomed way called religion and creed, and the rules known with certainty from the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus, such as that the One is the bringer into existence of the many, that the angel descends from heaven, that the world is preceded by non-existence and perishes after existence, and other rules that are certain in Islam, not in philosophy. To this alluded the one who said: the foundation of this science is adherence to the Book and the Sunnah, i.e., attachment to them and that its investigations are attributed to them and proceed according to their rules, as is the meaning of the attribution of beliefs to religion. And it was said: what is meant by the law of Islam are its principles from the Book, the Sunnah, consensus, and the rational that does not contradict them. In sum, its gist is that in all investigations one should preserve the religious rules and not contradict the certainties among them, proceeding according to the requirement of the view of discerning intellects, unlike the law of philosophy. Not that all investigations are truly in themselves attributed to Islam in reality; otherwise the definition would not apply to the speech of the anthropomorphists (mujassima), the Mu'tazila, the Khawarij, and those who follow.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage defines the subject matter of kalam (theology) and distinguishes it from philosophy (al-ilahi). The author begins by referencing an earlier point about criticism of kalam, then states the position of the early scholars (al-mutakaddimun): the subject of kalam is the existent insofar as it is (al-mawjud min haythu huwa), but it is distinguished from philosophy by the condition that investigation proceeds according to the law of Islam (qanun al-Islam), i.e., what is certainly known from religion such as the creation of multiplicity from one God, angels descending, and the world's temporality. He then explains his own approach: he delays certain discussions to maintain order in clarifying subject, issues, and goal. The early scholars made the subject the existent qua existent because all searches return to it. He quotes Imam al-Ghazali's description of the theologian's method: starting from the most general (the existent), dividing it into eternal and originated, then further divisions, leading to proofs of God's attributes, the permissibility of actions, prophethood, and miracles. After reason reaches its limit, one accepts revelation. The author then reinforces the distinction: philosophy also studies the existent qua existent, but kalam restricts it to investigations according to Islamic law—rules from Qur'an, Sunnah, and consensus, with examples. He cites a saying that the foundation is adherence to revealed sources. He clarifies that the definition of kalam as 'investigation on the law of Islam' applies even if the investigator errs, as long as they claim to follow Islamic law; otherwise, groups like the anthropomorphists, Mu'tazila, and Khawarij would be excluded, but they are still considered practitioners of kalam.

القديم والمحدث
الجوهر والعرض
المتكلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Kalam is the same as philosophy because both study the existent.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that kalam is distinguished by its method: it restricts investigation to what is known from Islamic law, whereas philosophy follows reason without that restriction.

What Is Kalam?
intermediate

Kalam's Methodological Foundation: The Law of Islam
Author explains the methodological restriction to Islamic law and its implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the law of Islam (Qur'an, Sunnah, consensus) functions as the defining principle of kalam, distinguishing it from philosophy and accommodating diverse theological schools.

Core Idea
Islamic law disciplines kalam's inquiry, not reason alone.

Having established that kalam shares its subject with philosophy, the author now clarifies the essential difference: kalam's investigations are bound by the law of Islam. This means the theologian must adhere to certainties from the Qur'an, Sunnah, and consensus, such as the creation of multiplicity from one God and the reality of angels. The passage also addresses a critical nuance: the definition applies even to those who err, as long as they claim to follow Islamic law, thus including groups like the Mu'tazila and Ash'aris.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the law of Islam as distinguishing factor
Start from 'Since the subject of the divine science in philosophy is the existent qua existent...' and read until the end. Notice how the author contrasts kalam with philosophy by emphasizing adherence to Islamic rules.
The phrase 'qanun al-Islam' is central.
2
Identify the examples of Islamic certainties
The passage lists examples: 'the One is the bringer into existence of the many', 'the angel descends from heaven', 'the world is preceded by non-existence'. These are doctrines that kalam accepts as premises, not conclusions of reason alone.
3
Understand the inclusivity clause
The author clarifies that the definition of kalam as 'investigation on the law of Islam' applies even to those who might be mistaken (like the anthropomorphists), as long as they intend to follow Islamic law. This is an important point about the scope of the discipline.
This distinguishes kalam as a historical discipline from 'true' theology.
4
Reflect on the role of reason within kalam
The passage mentions 'the rational that does not contradict them' as part of the law. This shows that reason is not excluded but subordinated to revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطعن فيه، فمحمول على ما إذا قصد التعصب في الدين، وإفساد عقائد المبتدئين، والتوريط في أودية الضلال بتزيين ما للفلسفة المقال. من قال المتقدمون على أن موضوعه الموجود من حيث هو، ويتميز عن الإلهي بكون البحث فيه على قانون الإسلام أي ما علم قطعاً من الدين كصدور الكثرة عن الواحد ونزول الملك من السماء وكون العالم محفوفاً بالعدم والفناء إلى غير ذلك مما تجزم به الملة دون الفلسفة لا ما هو الحق ولو ادعاء لمشاركة الفلسفة ككلام المخالف. أقول: أخر هذه المباحث مع تعلقها بالموضوع محافظة على انتظام الكلام في بيان الموضوع والمسائل والغاية فالمتقدمون من علماء الكلام جعلوا موضوعه الموجود بما هو موجود لرجوع مباحثه إليه على ما قال الإمام حجة الإسلام أن المتكلم ينظر في أعم الأشياء وهو الموجود فيقسمه إلى قديم ومحدث، والمحدث إلى جوهر وعرض والعرض إلى ما يشترط فيه الحياة كالعلم والقدرة وإلى ما لا يشترط كاللون والطعم ويقسم الجوهر إلى الحيوان والنبات والجماد، ويبين أن اختلافها بالأنواع أو بالأعراض، وينظر في القديم فيتبين أنه لا يتكثر ولا يتركب وأنه يتميز عن المحدث بصفات تجب له، وأمور تمتنع عليه، وأحكام تجوز في حقه من غير وجوب أو امتناع، ويبين أن أصل الفعل جائز عليه وأن العالم فعله الجائز فيفتقر بجوازه إلى محدث، وأنه قادر على بعث الرسل وعلى تعريف صدقهم بالمعجزات وأن هذا واقع وحينئذ ينتهي تصرف العقل ويأخذ في التلقي من النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام الثابت عنده صدقه ومقبول ما يقوله في الله تعالى وفي أمر المبدأ والمعاد. ولما كان موضوع العلم الإلهي من الفلسفة هو الموجود بما هو موجود وكان تمايز العلوم بتمايز الموضوعات قيد الموجود ههنا بحيثية كونه متعلقاً للمباحث الجارية على قانون الإسلام، فتميز الكلام عن الإلهي بأن البحث فيه إنما يكون على قانون الإسلام أي الطريقة المعهودة المسماة بالدين والملة، والقواعد المعلومة قطعاً من الكتاب والسنة والإجماع، مثل كون الواحد موجد للكثير، وكون الملك نازلاً من السماء، وكون العالم مسبوقاً بالعدم، وفانياً بعد الوجود، إلى غير ذلك من القواعد التي يقطع بها في الإسلام دون الفلسفة. وإلى هذا أشار من قال: الأصل في هذا العلم التمسك بالكتاب والسنة، أي التعلق بهما وكون مباحثه منتسبة إليهما جارية على قواعدهما على ما هو معنى انتساب العقائد إلى الدين. وقيل المراد بقانون الإسلام أصوله من الكتاب والسنة والإجماع والمعقول الذي لا يخالفها، وبالجملة فحاصله أن يحافظ في جميع المباحث على القواعد الشرعية ولا يخالف القطعيات منها جرياً على مقتضى نظر العقول الفاصرة على ما هو قانون الفلسفة، لا أن يكون جميع المباحث حقة في نفس الأمر منتسبة إلى الإسلام بالتحقيق، وإلا لما صدق التعريف على كلام المجسمة والمعتزلة والخوارج ومن يجري.
Criticism of it, then it is carried upon when one intends fanaticism in religion, corrupting the beliefs of beginners, and involving them in valleys of error by embellishing what belongs to philosophical discourse. The early scholars said that its subject is the existent insofar as it is, and it is distinguished from the divine science (al-ilahi) by the fact that investigation in it is according to the law of Islam (qanun al-Islam), i.e., what is known certainly from religion, such as the emanation of multiplicity from the One, the descent of the angel from heaven, and the world being surrounded by non-existence and annihilation, and other things that the religious community (milla) affirms with certainty, not philosophy — not what is true even if claimed to share with philosophy, like the speech of the opponent. I say: I postponed these discussions despite their connection to the subject to preserve the order of speech in explaining the subject, the issues, and the goal. The early scholars of kalam made its subject the existent qua existent because their investigations refer back to it, as the Imam, the Proof of Islam (al-Ghazali), said: the mutakallim (theologian) looks at the most general of things, which is the existent, and divides it into eternal and originated; the originated into substance and accident; the accident into what requires life, like knowledge and power, and what does not require it, like color and taste; and he divides substance into animal, plant, and inanimate; and he shows that their differences are by species or by accidents. And he looks at the eternal and then it becomes clear that it is not multiple nor composite, and that it is distinguished from the originated by attributes necessarily belonging to it, matters impossible for it, and judgments permissible for it without necessity or impossibility. And he shows that the origin of the action is permissible for Him, and that the world is His permissible action, so by its permissibility it needs an originator; and that He is able to send messengers and to verify their truthfulness by miracles, and that this actually occurs. Then the operation of the intellect ends and one begins to receive from the Prophet (peace be upon him), whose truthfulness is established, and what he says about God Almighty and about the matter of the beginning and the return is accepted. Since the subject of the divine science in philosophy is the existent qua existent, and the differentiation of sciences is by the differentiation of subjects, the existent is here restricted by the respect of its being related to investigations conducted according to the law of Islam. Thus kalam is distinguished from the divine science in that investigation in it is only according to the law of Islam, i.e., the accustomed way called religion and creed, and the rules known with certainty from the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus, such as that the One is the bringer into existence of the many, that the angel descends from heaven, that the world is preceded by non-existence and perishes after existence, and other rules that are certain in Islam, not in philosophy. To this alluded the one who said: the foundation of this science is adherence to the Book and the Sunnah, i.e., attachment to them and that its investigations are attributed to them and proceed according to their rules, as is the meaning of the attribution of beliefs to religion. And it was said: what is meant by the law of Islam are its principles from the Book, the Sunnah, consensus, and the rational that does not contradict them. In sum, its gist is that in all investigations one should preserve the religious rules and not contradict the certainties among them, proceeding according to the requirement of the view of discerning intellects, unlike the law of philosophy. Not that all investigations are truly in themselves attributed to Islam in reality; otherwise the definition would not apply to the speech of the anthropomorphists (mujassima), the Mu'tazila, the Khawarij, and those who follow.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage defines the subject matter of kalam (theology) and distinguishes it from philosophy (al-ilahi). The author begins by referencing an earlier point about criticism of kalam, then states the position of the early scholars (al-mutakaddimun): the subject of kalam is the existent insofar as it is (al-mawjud min haythu huwa), but it is distinguished from philosophy by the condition that investigation proceeds according to the law of Islam (qanun al-Islam), i.e., what is certainly known from religion such as the creation of multiplicity from one God, angels descending, and the world's temporality. He then explains his own approach: he delays certain discussions to maintain order in clarifying subject, issues, and goal. The early scholars made the subject the existent qua existent because all searches return to it. He quotes Imam al-Ghazali's description of the theologian's method: starting from the most general (the existent), dividing it into eternal and originated, then further divisions, leading to proofs of God's attributes, the permissibility of actions, prophethood, and miracles. After reason reaches its limit, one accepts revelation. The author then reinforces the distinction: philosophy also studies the existent qua existent, but kalam restricts it to investigations according to Islamic law—rules from Qur'an, Sunnah, and consensus, with examples. He cites a saying that the foundation is adherence to revealed sources. He clarifies that the definition of kalam as 'investigation on the law of Islam' applies even if the investigator errs, as long as they claim to follow Islamic law; otherwise, groups like the anthropomorphists, Mu'tazila, and Khawarij would be excluded, but they are still considered practitioners of kalam.

Key Terms
قانون الإسلام
الكتاب والسنة والإجماع
المجسمة
المعتزلة
الخوارج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Kalam is only for those who hold correct beliefs, and groups like the Mu'tazila are not considered practitioners of kalam.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that the definition applies even to erroneous groups (mujassima, Mu'tazila, Khawarij) as long as they intend to follow Islamic law, thus including them in the discipline.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary factor that distinguishes kalam from philosophy?
A) Kalam studies the existent while philosophy studies the non-existent.
B) Kalam restricts investigation to the law of Islam, while philosophy does not.
C) Kalam denies the use of reason.
D) Kalam only discusses attributes of God.

Key Takeaway
Kalam is defined not by its conclusions but by its method—investigation under the law of Islam—which allows for a diversity of theological positions within the tradition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you approach theological questions with the same commitment to the law of Islam as you do to legal rulings, or do you tend to rely on your own reasoning first? What would change if you truly made the Book and Sunnah the foundation of your theological investigations?
?
The passage shows that even groups considered deviant claim to follow Islamic law in their kalam. How do you ensure that your own beliefs are not simply a reflection of your preferred school or intellect, but are genuinely derived from the sources? What steps can you take to check yourself?
?
If kalam is defined by method rather than conclusions, how does that affect your view of those with different theological positions? Are you quick to dismiss them as outside Islam, or do you recognize that they may be sincerely following the same method?

What Is Kalam?
beginner
4 min
Distinction between Kalam and Divine Philosophy
Defines kalam's subject matter as existing being under Islamic law.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how kalam is distinguished from divine philosophy by its restriction to Islamic law.

Core Idea
Kalam studies being, but only as governed by Islamic law.

This passage from Sharh al-Maqasid explains what makes kalam unique among theological disciplines. While divine philosophy examines existence in general, kalam adds a crucial condition: it investigates being only insofar as it relates to Islamic law. This distinction shapes everything that follows in the study of kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins by describing the subject of divine philosophy before introducing the restriction.
2
Identify the key distinction
Find the sentence where the author states the difference between kalam and divine philosophy. Note the phrase 'according to the law of Islam'.
This is the central idea of the whole passage.
3
Examine the examples
Look at the examples given: the One creates the many, angels descend, the world is created and perishes. Ask yourself why these are specifically Islamic doctrines.
These examples are not accepted in philosophy but are certain in Islam.
4
Connect to the foundation principle
The passage ends by referencing a statement that the foundation is adherence to the Book and Sunnah. Reflect on how this reinforces the earlier distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما كان موضوع العلم الإلهي من الفلسفة هو الموجود بما هو موجود وكان تمايز العلوم بتمايز الموضوعات قيد الموجود ههنا بحيثية كونه متعلقاً للمباحث الجارية على قانون الإسلام، فتميز الكلام عن الإلهي بأن البحث فيه إنما يكون على قانون الإسلام أي الطريقة المعهودة المسماة بالدين والملة، والقواعد المعلومة قطعاً من الكتاب والسنة والإجماع، مثل كون الواحد موجد للكثير، وكون الملك نازلاً من السماء، وكون العالم مسبوقاً بالعدم، وفانياً بعد الوجود، إلى غير ذلك من القواعد التي يقطع بها في الإسلام دون الفلسفة. وإلى هذا أشار من قال : الأصل في هذا العلم التمسك بالكتاب والسنة، أي التعلق بهما وكون مباحثه منتسبة إليهما جارية على قواعدهما على ما هو معنى انتساب العقائد إلى الدين.
And when the subject of divine science (al-ʿilm al-ilāhī) from philosophy is being qua being, and sciences are distinguished by their subjects, being is restricted here by the aspect of its being related to investigations conducted according to the law of Islam (qānūn al-Islām). Thus kalam is distinguished from divine philosophy in that research in it is only according to the law of Islam, i.e., the customary path called religion and community (al-dīn wa al-milla), and the definitively known rules from the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus, such as that the One creates the many, that the angel descends from heaven, that the world is preceded by non-existence and perishes after existence, and other rules that are definitively held in Islam but not in philosophy. And this is what the one who said 'the foundation of this science is adherence to the Book and the Sunnah' referred to, i.e., attachment to them and that its investigations are attributed to them and follow their rules, as is the meaning of the attribution of beliefs to religion.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage defines and distinguishes the science of kalam from the philosophical discipline of divine science (Ilāhiyyāt). It begins by stating that the subject of divine philosophy is 'being qua being' (al-mawjūd bi-mā huwa mawjūd). Since sciences are distinguished by their subjects, kalam restricts the concept of 'being' by adding the condition that it is investigated according to the 'law of Islam' (qānūn al-Islām). This law refers to the accepted way of the religion and the community, and it consists of rules definitively known from the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus. The author gives examples: that the One God creates multiplicity, that angels descend from heaven, that the world is preceded by non-existence and will perish after existence. These are certain in Islam but not in philosophy. The passage then connects this to the statement of some scholars that 'the foundation of this science is adherence to the Book and the Sunnah,' meaning that all investigations are based on revelation and its principles, which is the meaning of attributing beliefs to religion.

Key Terms
الموجود بما هو موجود
قانون الإسلام
الكتاب والسنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think kalam is identical to philosophy.
Correction: This passage shows that kalam is restricted to Islamic principles, unlike philosophy which studies being without that restriction.

Checkpoint
What is the distinguishing feature of kalam compared to divine philosophy?
A) It studies being qua being
B) It studies being according to Islamic law
C) It denies philosophical proofs
D) It relies only on consensus

Key Takeaway
Kalam is distinguished from divine philosophy by investigating being only according to the principles of Islamic law.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you treat the Quran and Sunnah as the ultimate authority for your beliefs, even when your own reasoning or cultural assumptions pull you in a different direction? What is one area where you need to submit your intellect to revelation?
?
When you encounter a theological question (like the nature of God's actions), do you instinctively turn to Islamic sources or to your own logic? How would your approach change if you truly believed that kalam's method is 'only according to the law of Islam'?
?
The passage says that kalam follows rules 'definitively known from the Book, Sunnah, and consensus.' Which of your current beliefs are you absolutely certain are based on these sources, and which might be influenced by philosophy? Will you investigate the difference today?

Refuting the Objection on the Definition of Kalam
Refutation of an objection against the definition of kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the condition 'according to Islam' in the definition of kalam does not fail to distinguish it from other sciences, as the author refutes a common objection.

Core Idea
The definition's restriction is not meant to distinguish kalam by truth claim.

In this passage, the author addresses a potential flaw in the definition of kalam: that the restriction 'according to the law of Islam' does not set it apart from other fields like philosophy. He shows that whether interpreted as actual conformity to truth or as the researcher's belief, the restriction does not serve as a distinguishing mark, but the definition remains valid because its purpose is to define the subject matter, not to certify truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own argument come through before you interpret.
Notice the logical structure of objection and response.
2
Identify the objection and its two interpretations
The passage presents an objection that the restriction 'according to Islam' fails to distinguish kalam. The author then considers two possible meanings of 'according to Islam': actual conformity to truth, or the researcher's belief. Find these two cases.
Each case is introduced with 'إن أريد' (if intended).
3
Understand why neither interpretation distinguishes kalam
For the first meaning, the author argues that everyone claims truth, so it's not distinguishing, and it would exclude false statements even if they are about kalam. For the second meaning, both kalam and philosophy share that characteristic, so again no distinction. Follow the reasoning.
4
Reflect on the purpose of the definition
Consider why the definition is still valid despite not distinguishing by truth claim. The author implies that the definition focuses on the subject matter (issues of kalam) rather than epistemic claims.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مجراهم وعلى هذا لا يرد الاعتراض بأن قانون الإسلام ما هو الحق من مسائل الكلام فإن أريد الحقية والانتساب إلى الإسلام بحسب الواقع لم يصلح هذا القيد لتميز الكلام عن غيره، لأنه ليس لازماً بيناً، إذ كل من المتكلم وغيره يدعي حقية مقاله، ولم يصدق التعريف على كلام المخالف لبطلان كثير من أنه كلام وفاقاً، وإن أريد بحسب اعتقاد الباحث حقاً كان أو باطلاً، لم يتميز الكلام بهذا القيد عن الإلهي لاشتراكهما في ذلك
Their way [of proceeding] and upon this the objection is not raised that the law of Islam is what is true from the issues of kalam. For if by truth and attribution to Islam is meant according to reality, this restriction is not suitable to distinguish kalam from others, because it is not a necessary self-evident [characteristic], since every one—both the mutakallim and others—claims the truth of his statement. And the definition would not apply to the speech of the opponent because much of it is false, even if it is speech by agreement. And if it is meant according to the belief of the researcher, whether true or false, then kalam is not distinguished by this restriction from al-ilahi (philosophical theology) because both share in that.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage refutes a potential objection against the definition of kalam. The objection is that adding the condition 'according to the law of Islam' does not effectively distinguish kalam from other disciplines, especially philosophy (al-ilahi). The author explains that if 'according to Islam' means actually conforming to Islamic truth, then the definition fails because every scholar claims truth for his own statements, and the definition would not apply to false statements even if they are about kalam. If it means according to the researcher's belief, then both kalam and philosophy share that characteristic, so no distinction is achieved. Thus the objection is not valid because the definition is not meant to distinguish in that way.

Key Terms
قيد
حقية
انتساب إلى الإسلام
لازم بين
كلام المخالف
الإلهي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The condition 'according to Islam' in the definition of kalam is meant to distinguish kalam from all other sciences by its truth claim.
Correction: The author shows that this condition does not serve as an epistemic distinguisher; the definition focuses on the subject matter (issues of kalam) and remains valid regardless of whether it epistemically separates kalam from other fields.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why does the condition 'according to Islam' not distinguish kalam from other sciences when taken in the sense of actual truth?
A) Because all sciences claim to be true.
B) Because kalam is not restricted to Islam.
C) Because the definition would be too narrow.
D) Because philosophy also studies God.

Key Takeaway
The condition 'according to Islam' in the definition of kalam does not need to serve as an epistemic distinguisher; the definition is valid as a description of the subject matter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you examine your own beliefs, do you assume they are 'true' and 'Islamic' without distinguishing the subject matter from the claim? How does this passage force you to separate what you study from how you certify it?
?
In debates about religion, you often assert that your position is 'the truth of Islam.' But this passage warns that such a claim does not define the field. Will you now be more careful about whether you are doing kalam or merely claiming truth?
?
The condition 'according to Islam' is not a badge of correctness but a description of domain. In your own learning, do you treat your acquired knowledge as a tool for truth or as a shield for your ego? What would change if you focused on the subject matter rather than the label?
